         </a>

      <p>
       <b>
        Rosario
       </b>
       (
       <small>
        Spanish pronunciation:
       </small>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">
         [roˈsaɾjo]
        </a>
       </span>
       ) is the largest city in the
       <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Argentina" title="Provinces of Argentina">
        province
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe_Province" title="Santa Fe Province">
        Santa Fe
       </a>
       , in central
       <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">
        Argentina
       </a>
       . It is located 300 km (186 mi) northwest of
       <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">
        Buenos Aires
       </a>
       , on the western shore of the
       <a href="/wiki/Paran%C3%A1_River" title="Paraná River">
        Paraná River
       </a>
       . Rosario is the third most populous city in the country, and is also the most populous city in Argentina that is not a provincial capital. With a growing and important
       <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">
        metropolitan area
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Greater_Rosario" title="Greater Rosario">
        Greater Rosario
       </a>
       has an estimated population of 1,276,000 as of 2012
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eph_5-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-eph-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       One of its main attractions includes the
       <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">
        neoclassical architecture
       </a>
       that has been retained over the centuries in hundreds of residences, houses, and public buildings.
      </p>
      <p>
       Rosario is the head city of the
       <a href="/wiki/Rosario_Department" title="Rosario Department">
        Rosario Department
       </a>
       and is located at the heart of the major
       <a href="/wiki/Industry" title="Industry">
        industrial corridor
       </a>
       in Argentina. The city is a major
       <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport" title="Rail transport">
        railroad
       </a>
       terminal and the shipping center for north-eastern Argentina. Ships reach the city via the Paraná River, which allows the existence of a 10-metre-deep (34 ft)
       <a href="/wiki/Port" title="Port">
        port
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Rosario" title="Port of Rosario">
        Port of Rosario
       </a>
       is subject to
       <a href="/wiki/Silt" title="Silt">
        silting
       </a>
       and must be
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dredge" title="Dredge">
        dredged
       </a>
       periodically.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Export" title="Export">
        Exports
       </a>
       include
       <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">
        wheat
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Flour" title="Flour">
        flour
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hay" title="Hay">
        hay
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Linseed" title="Linseed">
        linseed
       </a>
       and other
       <a href="/wiki/Vegetable_oil" title="Vegetable oil">
        vegetable oils
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">
        corn
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">
        sugar
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lumber" title="Lumber">
        lumber
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Meat" title="Meat">
        meat
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hide_(skin)" title="Hide (skin)">
        hides
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Wool" title="Wool">
        wool
       </a>
       . Manufactured goods include flour, sugar, meat products, and other foodstuffs. The
       <a href="/wiki/Rosario-Victoria_Bridge" title="Rosario-Victoria Bridge">
        Rosario-Victoria Bridge
       </a>
       , opened in 2004, spans the Paraná River, connecting Rosario with the city of
       <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_Entre_R%C3%ADos" title="Victoria, Entre Ríos">
        Victoria
       </a>
       , across the
       <a href="/wiki/Paran%C3%A1_Delta" title="Paraná Delta">
        Paraná Delta
       </a>
       . Because it plays a critical role in agricultural commerce, the city finds itself at the center of a continuing debate over taxes levied on big-ticket agricultural goods such as soy.
      </p>
      <p>
       Along with
       <a href="/wiki/Paran%C3%A1,_Entre_R%C3%ADos" title="Paraná, Entre Ríos">
        Paraná
       </a>
       , Rosario is one of the few Argentine cities that cannot point to a particular individual as its founder. The city's patron is the "
       <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_the_Rosary" title="Our Lady of the Rosary">
        Virgin of the Rosary
       </a>
       ", whose feast day is October 7. The asteroid
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/14812_Rosario" title="14812 Rosario">
        14812 Rosario
       </a>
       was named in its honor.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Notable people from Rosario include the
       <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary" title="Revolutionary">
        revolutionary
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Che_Guevara" title="Che Guevara">
        Che Guevara
       </a>
       ;
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soccer" title="Soccer">
        football
       </a>
       players
       <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Messi" title="Lionel Messi">
        Lionel Messi
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/%C3%81ngel_Di_Mar%C3%ADa" title="Ángel Di María">
        Ángel Di María
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Maxi_Rodr%C3%ADguez" title="Maxi Rodríguez">
        Maximiliano Rodríguez
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mauro_Icardi" title="Mauro Icardi">
        Mauro Icardi
       </a>
       ; football coaches
       <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A9sar_Luis_Menotti" title="César Luis Menotti">
        César Luis Menotti
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Marcelo_Bielsa" title="Marcelo Bielsa">
        Marcelo Bielsa
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Gerardo_Martino" title="Gerardo Martino">
        Gerardo Martino
       </a>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/Field_hockey" title="Field hockey">
        field hockey
       </a>
       player
       <a href="/wiki/Luciana_Aymar" title="Luciana Aymar">
        Luciana Aymar
       </a>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">
        rugby union
       </a>
       players
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Imhoff" title="Juan Imhoff">
        Juan Imhoff
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_Senatore" title="Leonardo Senatore">
        Leonardo Senatore
       </a>
       ; actor/comedian
       <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Olmedo" title="Alberto Olmedo">
        Alberto Olmedo
       </a>
       and actress
       <a href="/wiki/Libertad_Lamarque" title="Libertad Lamarque">
        Libertad Lamarque
       </a>
       ; jazz composer
       <a href="/wiki/Gato_Barbieri" title="Gato Barbieri">
        Gato Barbieri
       </a>
       ; cartoonist
       <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Fontanarrosa" title="Roberto Fontanarrosa">
        Roberto Fontanarrosa
       </a>
       ; singer-songwriter
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fito_Paez" title="Fito Paez">
        Fito Paez
       </a>
       ; painter
       <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Berni" title="Antonio Berni">
        Antonio Berni
       </a>
       , operatic tenor
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Cura" title="José Cura">
        José Cura
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and model
       <a href="/wiki/Valeria_Mazza" title="Valeria Mazza">
        Valeria Mazza
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

           17
          </span>
          <span class="toctext">
           See also
          </span>
         </a>
        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-51">

          </span>

        </li>
       </ul>
      </div>
      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Rosario" title="History of Rosario">
        History of Rosario
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_settlement">
        Early settlement
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early settlement">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ciudad_del_Rosario_de_Santa_Fe_(1858).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2502" data-file-width="3296" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Ciudad_del_Rosario_de_Santa_Fe_%281858%29.jpg/200px-Ciudad_del_Rosario_de_Santa_Fe_%281858%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Ciudad_del_Rosario_de_Santa_Fe_%281858%29.jpg/300px-Ciudad_del_Rosario_de_Santa_Fe_%281858%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Ciudad_del_Rosario_de_Santa_Fe_%281858%29.jpg/400px-Ciudad_del_Rosario_de_Santa_Fe_%281858%29.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ciudad_del_Rosario_de_Santa_Fe_(1858).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map of the city of Rosario circa 1877
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Puerto_Rosario_1868.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2142" data-file-width="1942" height="221" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Puerto_Rosario_1868.jpg/200px-Puerto_Rosario_1868.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Puerto_Rosario_1868.jpg/300px-Puerto_Rosario_1868.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Puerto_Rosario_1868.jpg/400px-Puerto_Rosario_1868.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Puerto_Rosario_1868.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Rosario port area in 1888
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Even though the city did not have a clear foundation date or any official acknowledgement thereof, most commentators state that Rosario was founded on 7 October 1793 with a local population of 457 inhabitants.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Nonetheless the town was officially declared as
       <i>
        city
       </i>
       on 3 August 1852, at the time it was known as
       <i>
        <b>
         Pago de los Arroyos
        </b>
       </i>
       , that is, "land of the
       <a href="/wiki/Stream" title="Stream">
        streams
       </a>
       ", a reference to the several small rivers that traverse the southern region of Santa Fe, like the
       <a href="/wiki/Ludue%C3%B1a_Stream" title="Ludueña Stream">
        Ludueña Stream
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Saladillo_Stream" title="Saladillo Stream">
        Saladillo Stream
       </a>
       and others, emptying into the Paraná River. In 1689, captain Luis Romero de Pineda received part of the lands of the Pago de los Arroyos by royal decree, as payment for services to the Spanish Crown. Before that, the area was originally inhabited by
       <a href="/wiki/Calchaqu%C3%AD" title="Calchaquí">
        Calchaquí
       </a>
       tribes in
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_Reductions" title="Indian Reductions">
         reducciones
        </a>
       </i>
       , a kind of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mission_(Christian)" title="Mission (Christian)">
        missions
       </a>
       founded by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Franciscan" title="Franciscan">
        Franciscans
       </a>
       . These missions were ultimately attacked and destroyed by hostile tribes of the
       <a href="/wiki/Gran_Chaco" title="Gran Chaco">
        Chaco
       </a>
       region.
      </p>
      <p>
       Romero de Pineda established the first permanent settlement, an
       <i>
        estancia
       </i>
       — intended as farmland, not as a town. In 1719 the
       <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">
        Jesuits
       </a>
       bought another part and established
       <i>
        Estancia San Miguel
       </i>
       . The area was still so scarcely populated that it had no central authority; it was ruled from the provincial capital (
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe,_Argentina" title="Santa Fe, Argentina">
        Santa Fe
       </a>
       ), and in turn from Buenos Aires.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1724, another colonial settlement was initiated by Santiago de Montenegro, who set up a mill, drew plans for the future town, built a
       <a href="/wiki/Chapel" title="Chapel">
        chapel
       </a>
       , and was appointed
       <a href="/wiki/Mayor" title="Mayor">
        mayor
       </a>
       in 1751. The area of control of this local government extended northward from today's Rosario; only in 1784 was it divided into two smaller jurisdictions.
      </p>
      <p>
       On February 27, 1812, General
       <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Belgrano" title="Manuel Belgrano">
        Manuel Belgrano
       </a>
       raised the newly created
       <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Argentina" title="Flag of Argentina">
        Argentine flag
       </a>
       on the shores of the Paraná, for the first time. Because of this, Rosario is known as the "Cradle of the Argentine Flag". The
       <a href="/wiki/National_Flag_Memorial_(Argentina)" title="National Flag Memorial (Argentina)">
        National Flag Memorial
       </a>
       marks the occasion.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="19th_century">
        19th century
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 19th century">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aduana_Rosario.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="1728" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Aduana_Rosario.jpg/200px-Aduana_Rosario.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Aduana_Rosario.jpg/300px-Aduana_Rosario.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Aduana_Rosario.jpg/400px-Aduana_Rosario.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aduana_Rosario.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Rosario's old Customs Office, on Belgrano Avenue
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The province of Santa Fe greatly suffered the civil war that afflicted Argentina after 1820. Demographic growth was relatively slow. During this period, Rosario was a small settlement and a stop on the way from Santa Fe City to Buenos Aires. In 1823 it was elevated to the category of "village" (
       <i>
        Ilustre y Fiel Villa del Rosario
       </i>
       ).
       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin" title="Charles Darwin">
        Charles Darwin
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Voyage_of_the_Beagle" title="The Voyage of the Beagle">
        travelled
       </a>
       through the area in 1832 and described Rosario as "a large town" with about 2,000 residents. In 1841
       <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Rosario" title="Port of Rosario">
        its port
       </a>
       was shut off to
       <a href="/wiki/International_trade" title="International trade">
        foreign trade
       </a>
       by a decree of the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Caudillo" title="Caudillo">
         caudillo
        </a>
       </i>
       and Governor of Buenos Aires,
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Manuel_de_Rosas" title="Juan Manuel de Rosas">
        Juan Manuel de Rosas
       </a>
       which banned navigation of the Paraná and the
       <a href="/wiki/Paraguay_River" title="Paraguay River">
        Paraguay
       </a>
       rivers to non-Argentine vessels.
      </p>
      <p>
       On 25 December 1851, a small group of locals and the military guard of the city declared their support for the rival
       <i>
        caudillo
       </i>
       <a href="/wiki/Justo_Jos%C3%A9_de_Urquiza" title="Justo José de Urquiza">
        Justo José de Urquiza
       </a>
       . As a reward for their participation in the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Caseros" title="Battle of Caseros">
        Battle of Caseros
       </a>
       , triumphant Urquiza wrote to the governor of Santa Fe on 9 June 1852 asking for Rosario to be granted city status. Governor
       <a href="/wiki/Domingo_Crespo" title="Domingo Crespo">
        Domingo Crespo
       </a>
       justified the request at the provincial legislative body, marking the geographically strategic position of the town for national and international trade, and on 5 August Rosario was formally declared a city.
      </p>
      <p>
       Urquiza opened up the river for free international trade. The city's economy and population expanded at an accelerated rate. By 1880, Rosario had become the first
       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_trade_of_Argentina" title="Foreign trade of Argentina">
        export outlet of Argentina
       </a>
       . By 1887 it had about 50,000 inhabitants, of which 40% were
       <a href="/wiki/Great_European_immigration_wave_to_Argentina" title="Great European immigration wave to Argentina">
        immigrants
       </a>
       , who brought new ideas from Europe and started turning Rosario into a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Political_progressivism" title="Political progressivism">
        politically progressive
       </a>
       city (contrasting with the more
       <a href="/wiki/Conservatism" title="Conservatism">
        conservative
       </a>
       , aristocratic Santa Fe).
      </p>
      <p>
       During part of the second half of the 19th century, there was a movement promoting that the city of Rosario become the capital of the republic.
       <a href="/wiki/Ovidio_Lagos" title="Ovidio Lagos">
        Ovidio Lagos
       </a>
       , founder of the oldest Argentine newspaper,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/La_Capital" title="La Capital">
         La Capital
        </a>
       </i>
       , was one of the strongest defenders of this idea (
       <a href="/wiki/Ovidio_Lagos_Avenue" title="Ovidio Lagos Avenue">
        one of the main avenues in Rosario
       </a>
       now carries his name). Rosario was indeed declared the federal capital in three occasions, but each time the law received a veto of the Executive Branch (once by
       <a href="/wiki/Bartolom%C3%A9_Mitre" title="Bartolomé Mitre">
        Bartolomé Mitre
       </a>
       and twice by
       <a href="/wiki/Domingo_Faustino_Sarmiento" title="Domingo Faustino Sarmiento">
        Domingo Faustino Sarmiento
       </a>
       ). In the last 15 years of the 19th century, the city more than doubled its population, in part due to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Immigration_in_Argentina" title="Immigration in Argentina">
        immigration
       </a>
       . In 1911 the French-owned railway company
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ferrocarril_Rosario_y_Puerto_Belgrano" title="Ferrocarril Rosario y Puerto Belgrano">
        Ferrocarril Rosario y Puerto Belgrano
       </a>
       opened a line between Rosario and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puerto_Belgrano" title="Puerto Belgrano">
        Puerto Belgrano
       </a>
       , Argentina's main naval base. By 1926, Rosario had 407,000 inhabitants, 47% of them foreign, many coming from Europe in the wake of World War I.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_history">
        Contemporary history
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Contemporary history">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Monumento_a_la_Bandera,_Rosario.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3664" data-file-width="2748" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Monumento_a_la_Bandera%2C_Rosario.jpg/200px-Monumento_a_la_Bandera%2C_Rosario.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Monumento_a_la_Bandera%2C_Rosario.jpg/300px-Monumento_a_la_Bandera%2C_Rosario.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Monumento_a_la_Bandera%2C_Rosario.jpg/400px-Monumento_a_la_Bandera%2C_Rosario.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Monumento_a_la_Bandera,_Rosario.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/National_Flag_Memorial_(Argentina)" title="National Flag Memorial (Argentina)">
          National Flag Memorial
         </a>
         , downtown Rosario
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1946 Rosario massively supported
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Per%C3%B3n" title="Juan Perón">
        Juan Perón
       </a>
       's rise to power. The city received the benefits of the
       <a href="/wiki/Nationalization" title="Nationalization">
        nationalization
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Subsidy" title="Subsidy">
        subsidizing
       </a>
       of many industries. Perón
       <a href="/wiki/Revoluci%C3%B3n_Libertadora" title="Revolución Libertadora">
        was deposed in 1955
       </a>
       . In 1969 workers and students took the streets to protest against the dictatorship (
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Rosariazo" title="Rosariazo">
         Rosariazo
        </a>
       </i>
       ). During the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Reorganization_Process" title="National Reorganization Process">
        dictatorship
       </a>
       started in 1976, hundreds of citizens were "
       <a href="/wiki/Forced_disappearance" title="Forced disappearance">
        disappeared
       </a>
       " by the government.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1983 Argentina returned to democratic rule but
       <a href="/wiki/Hyperinflation" title="Hyperinflation">
        hyperinflation
       </a>
       caused the economic collapse of the country in 1989. In Rosario there were
       <a href="/wiki/1989_riots_in_Argentina" title="1989 riots in Argentina">
        riots
       </a>
       with episodes of looting. Under the
       <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Menem" title="Carlos Menem">
        Menem administration
       </a>
       the situation became worse as the industrial sector of the city was dismantled by foreign competition and agricultural exports stagnated. In 1995
       <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">
        unemployment
       </a>
       in the area reached 21.1%, and a large part of Rosario's population fell below the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Poverty_line" title="Poverty line">
        poverty line
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Since the recovery of the
       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Argentina" title="Economy of Argentina">
        national economy
       </a>
       that followed the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Argentine_economic_crisis_(1999%E2%80%932002)" title="Argentine economic crisis (1999–2002)">
        2001 collapse
       </a>
       , Rosario's economic situation has improved. The boom in agricultural exports has caused a large increase in consumer spending and investment. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_of_Argentina" title="Socialist Party of Argentina">
        Socialist Party
       </a>
       has won mayoral races in the city in every election since 1989, when Councilman
       <a href="/wiki/H%C3%A9ctor_Cavallero" title="Héctor Cavallero">
        Héctor Cavallero
       </a>
       was elected. His successor,
       <a href="/wiki/Hermes_Binner" title="Hermes Binner">
        Hermes Binner
       </a>
       (elected in 1995), was elected
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Governor_of_Santa_Fe" title="Governor of Santa Fe">
        Governor of Santa Fe
       </a>
       in 2007 and became the runner-up in the
       <a href="/wiki/Argentine_general_election,_2011" title="Argentine general election, 2011">
        2011 presidential election
       </a>
       on the
       <a href="/wiki/Broad_Progressive_Front_(Argentina)" title="Broad Progressive Front (Argentina)">
        FAP
       </a>
       ticket. Mayor
       <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Lifschitz" title="Miguel Lifschitz">
        Miguel Lifschitz
       </a>
       's administration, elected in 2007, took advantage of the economic boom to invest heavily in
       <a href="/wiki/Public_works" title="Public works">
        public works
       </a>
       , as well as in public health (which takes up about a quarter of the whole
       <a href="/wiki/Budget" title="Budget">
        budget
       </a>
       ). Mayor
       <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B3nica_Fein" title="Mónica Fein">
        Mónica Fein
       </a>
       became, in 2011, the first Socialist woman elected mayor in Argentine history.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_images">

         <div class="thumb" style="width: 72.666666666667px;">

          </span>
          <div style="margin:0px auto;">
           <span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_images">
            <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hotel_Savoy_Rosario_(postal_FR).jpg">
             <img alt="" data-file-height="699" data-file-width="424" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Hotel_Savoy_Rosario_%28postal_FR%29.jpg/109px-Hotel_Savoy_Rosario_%28postal_FR%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Hotel_Savoy_Rosario_%28postal_FR%29.jpg/164px-Hotel_Savoy_Rosario_%28postal_FR%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Hotel_Savoy_Rosario_%28postal_FR%29.jpg/218px-Hotel_Savoy_Rosario_%28postal_FR%29.jpg 2x" width="73"/>
            </a>
           </span>
          </div>
         </div>

      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_images">
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Government">
         Government
        </span>
        <span class="mw-editsection">
         <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
          [
         </span>
         <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Government">
          edit
         </a>
         <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
          ]
         </span>
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Rosario" title="Government of Rosario">
        Government of Rosario
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Palacio_de_los_Leones_5.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="2304" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Palacio_de_los_Leones_5.jpg/180px-Palacio_de_los_Leones_5.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Palacio_de_los_Leones_5.jpg/270px-Palacio_de_los_Leones_5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Palacio_de_los_Leones_5.jpg/360px-Palacio_de_los_Leones_5.jpg 2x" width="180"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Palacio_de_los_Leones_5.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <i>
          Palacio de los Leones
         </i>
         (City Hall).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Rosario is ruled by an executive branch represented by a
       <a href="/wiki/Mayor" title="Mayor">
        mayor
       </a>
       (seat:
       <a href="/wiki/Palacio_de_los_Leones" title="Palacio de los Leones">
        Palacio de los Leones
       </a>
       ), and a legislative branch, consisting of a Deliberative Council (seat:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palacio_Vassallo" title="Palacio Vassallo">
        Palacio Vassallo
       </a>
       ). The mayor is elected for a four-year term, and the Council renews half of its 21 members every two years.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Municipal_Centre_District_.28CMD.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Municipal_Centre_District_(CMD)">
        Municipal Centre District (CMD)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Municipal Centre District (CMD)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Since 1997, a municipal program of decentralization of legislative activities was carried out, materialized in 6 Municipal Centres of District (Centre, North, South, West, Northwest and Southwest).
      </p>
      <p>
       The city is divided into six large administrative
       <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Rosario" title="Districts of Rosario">
        districts
       </a>
       (Center, North, Northwest, West, Southwest, and South), with Municipal District Centers that provide services to the population.
      </p>
      <p>
       For years, local people and institutions have been pushing the provincial government to grant Rosario the status of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autonomous_entity#Argentina" title="Autonomous entity">
        Autonomous City
       </a>
       . Some, with the sponsorship of the governors of Santa Fe, Entre Ríos and Córdoba as well as other important politicians, have put forward a legislative project to move the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Argentine_National_Congress" title="Argentine National Congress">
        National Congress
       </a>
       to Rosario, to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Decentralisation" title="Decentralisation">
        decentralize
       </a>
       the national government.
      </p>
      <p>
       Since the return to democracy in 1983, the Mayors of Rosario were
       <a href="/wiki/Horacio_Usandizaga" title="Horacio Usandizaga">
        Horacio Usandizaga
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/H%C3%A9ctor_Cavallero" title="Héctor Cavallero">
        Héctor Cavallero
       </a>
       (standing in for Usandizaga, then re-elected),
       <a href="/wiki/Hermes_Binner" title="Hermes Binner">
        Hermes Binner
       </a>
       (re-elected once),
       <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Lifschitz" title="Miguel Lifschitz">
        Miguel Lifschitz
       </a>
       (re-elected once), and, since December 2011,
       <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B3nica_Fein" title="Mónica Fein">
        Mónica Fein
       </a>
       . From Cavallero on (1989), the mayor has been a member of the
       <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_(Argentina)" title="Socialist Party (Argentina)">
        Socialist Party
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The city does not have a
       <a href="/wiki/Police" title="Police">
        police
       </a>
       force of its own (it is served by the provincial police), but in 2004 it pioneered the creation of a special patrol force of unarmed officers called
       <i>
        Guardia Urbana Municipal
       </i>
       ("Municipal Urban Guard") which was imitated later by
       <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">
        Buenos Aires
       </a>
       and other cities.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Perpetuo_Socorro_Rosario_3.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="1728" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Perpetuo_Socorro_Rosario_3.jpg/170px-Perpetuo_Socorro_Rosario_3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Perpetuo_Socorro_Rosario_3.jpg/255px-Perpetuo_Socorro_Rosario_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Perpetuo_Socorro_Rosario_3.jpg/340px-Perpetuo_Socorro_Rosario_3.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Perpetuo_Socorro_Rosario_3.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <i>
          Parroquia del Perpetuo Socorro
         </i>
         , a church at Lisandro de la Torre district
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Municipal_statistics">
        Municipal statistics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Municipal statistics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The municipality of Rosario comprises 178.69 square kilometres (69.0 sq mi), of which 117.2 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (45 sq mi) are urbanized, in 6,306 housing blocks. Of this area, 9.3 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (3.6 sq mi), 5.3% is devoted to green spaces (parks, boulevards, plazas), which gives over 10 m
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       of green space per inhabitant.
      </p>
      <p>
       Electric power is supplied to the whole urban area and running water reaches 97% of the population (about 350,000 homes). Natural gas is provided to 227,152 homes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       With the recovery of the national economy since 2002, the city experienced a real-estate boom. In the period 2003–2006, the construction sector added 2 million m
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       , investing about $900 million. Despite this increased supply, both price and rent have increased sharply compared to the values during the 1990s.
      </p>
      <p>
       According to experts, this growth was propelled by the increased purchasing power of farmers around Rosario, helped by competitive exports, and the overall preference for safer investment options.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Health">
        Health
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Health">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Rosario has a number of public health centers: 5 municipal hospitals (including a
       <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_hospital" title="Children's hospital">
        children's hospital
       </a>
       and an emergency hospital/
       <a href="/wiki/Trauma_center" title="Trauma center">
        trauma center
       </a>
       ) and a municipal outpatient-only center, plus 2 large provincial hospitals (
       <a href="/wiki/Hospital_Provincial_de_Rosario" title="Hospital Provincial de Rosario">
        Hospital Provincial
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hospital_Provincial_del_Centenario_(Rosario)" title="Hospital Provincial del Centenario (Rosario)">
        Hospital Centenario
       </a>
       ), and their associated
       <a href="/wiki/Primary_care" title="Primary care">
        primary care
       </a>
       centers in the city proper and its metropolitan area.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Argentina" title="Economy of Argentina">
        Economy of Argentina
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bolsa_de_Comercio_Rosario.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3598" data-file-width="4372" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Bolsa_de_Comercio_Rosario.jpg/200px-Bolsa_de_Comercio_Rosario.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Bolsa_de_Comercio_Rosario.jpg/300px-Bolsa_de_Comercio_Rosario.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Bolsa_de_Comercio_Rosario.jpg/400px-Bolsa_de_Comercio_Rosario.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bolsa_de_Comercio_Rosario.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Bolsa de Comercio Rosario: The Rosario Stock Exchange
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Rosario is the main epicentre of a metropolitan region whose economy is based on services and industry, generating the second largest urban
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gross_state_product" title="Gross state product">
        gross regional product
       </a>
       of Argentina, after Greater Buenos Aires.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The principal manufacturing sector is the
       <a href="/wiki/Industry" title="Industry">
        agro industry
       </a>
       , whose industries are placed in the northern and southern areas of the
       <a href="/wiki/Greater_Rosario" title="Greater Rosario">
        Greater Rosario
       </a>
       ; the investments over the last decade have transformed Rosario into a major role of processing oil of the world
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Many other sectors contribute to the diversified industrial offerings of the city. Rosario and its metropolitan area produce 20% of the cars, 4% of the domestic refrigerators, 80% of the machinery for the food industry and 100% of the auto bodies for long distance buses made in Argentina.
      </p>
      <p>
       Other important sectors include the petrochemical sector, with three plants located in the suburbs of San Lorenzo and Port San Martin; the chemistry sector, with plants for sulphuric acid, fertilizers, resins and other products; the cellulose industry; the meat industry; ironworks; auto parts; the plants and equipment for bottled oil; agricultural machinery; and the materials and equipment for the construction industry. Worldwide international companies settled in Rosario include, among others,
       <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">
        General Motors
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cargill" title="Cargill">
        Cargill
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Unilever" title="Unilever">
        Unilever
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/John_Deere" title="John Deere">
        John Deere
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petrobr%C3%A1s" title="Petrobrás">
        Petrobrás
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Chemical_Industries" title="Imperial Chemical Industries">
        ICI
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dow_Chemical" title="Dow Chemical">
        Dow
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tenneco" title="Tenneco">
        Tenneco
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mahle_GmbH" title="Mahle GmbH">
        Mahle
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The main financial bank at the city of Rosario is the
       <a href="/wiki/Municipal_Bank_of_Rosario" title="Municipal Bank of Rosario">
        Municipal Bank of Rosario
       </a>
       . Its central offices are located in the financial district, on
       <a href="/wiki/San_Mart%C3%ADn_Street_(Rosario)" title="San Martín Street (Rosario)">
        San Martín St.
       </a>
       , and there are several additional offices throughout the city. It is focused on
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Small_and_medium_enterprise" title="Small and medium enterprise">
        small and medium enterprises
       </a>
       and other organizations, especially through
       <a href="/wiki/Microcredit" title="Microcredit">
        micro credits
       </a>
       , and may be considered an "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethical_bank" title="Ethical bank">
        ethical bank
       </a>
       ."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Puente_Rosario-Victoria_2.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Puente_Rosario-Victoria_2.jpg/200px-Puente_Rosario-Victoria_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Puente_Rosario-Victoria_2.jpg/300px-Puente_Rosario-Victoria_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Puente_Rosario-Victoria_2.jpg/400px-Puente_Rosario-Victoria_2.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Puente_Rosario-Victoria_2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Wood chips carrier Racer on the
         <a href="/wiki/Paran%C3%A1_River" title="Paraná River">
          Paraná River
         </a>
         , just coming under the Rosario-Victoria Bridge
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Municipal Bank was founded in 1896 to support the financial needs of the citizens and small businesses in the highly productive region of southern Santa Fe Province, centered in Rosario. At the time, the city had around 92,000 inhabitants and was already
       <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Rosario" title="Port of Rosario">
        the most important port
       </a>
       on the Paraná River. The idea of creating a municipal financial institution was expressed in 1893 by Mayor Floduardo Grandoli, citing the proliferation of "centers of
       <a href="/wiki/Usury" title="Usury">
        usury
       </a>
       " that exploited those in need of credit, especially the poor (something not addressed by the profile of the
       <a href="/wiki/New_Bank_of_Santa_Fe" title="New Bank of Santa Fe">
        Provincial Bank of Santa Fe
       </a>
       , which granted loans only to demonstrably solvent persons). Acting on this, the municipal Counseling Commission passed a bill (on 1 February 1895) dictating an "Organic Charter of the Municipal Bank of Loans and Savings Accounts;" the bank opened exactly one year later.
      </p>
      <p>
       The seat of the bank was moved in 1905. Its name was changed to its present form on 14 May 1940 by a municipal bill. Its location was moved again, for the last time so far, in 1986. Following some political controversy, the bank in 2006 was capitalized by the municipality in order to comply with new regulations dictated by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Banco_Central_de_la_Rep%C3%BAblica_Argentina" title="Banco Central de la República Argentina">
        Central Bank
       </a>
       , and transformed into a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joint_stock_company" title="Joint stock company">
        joint stock company
       </a>
       , with only 1% of the stock belonging to the municipal state. A special clause was added, dictating that this minimum share is unchangeable, so as to prevent hypothetical attempts at
       <a href="/wiki/Privatization" title="Privatization">
        privatization
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Rosario_Board_of_Trade" title="Rosario Board of Trade">
        Rosario Board of Trade
       </a>
       hosts the country's largest
       <a href="/wiki/Commodity" title="Commodity">
        commodity
       </a>
       market, dealing in cereals and oilseeds, and also the largest
       <a href="/wiki/Futures_exchange" title="Futures exchange">
        futures exchange
       </a>
       (ROFEX). The banking sector includes the state-owned
       <a href="/wiki/Municipal_Bank_of_Rosario" title="Municipal Bank of Rosario">
        Municipal Bank of Rosario
       </a>
       , with branches and offices throughout the city, and the central branch of the
       <a href="/wiki/New_Bank_of_Santa_Fe" title="New Bank of Santa Fe">
        New Bank of Santa Fe
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The largest technological center in Argentina –
       <a href="/wiki/Rosario_Technological_Center" title="Rosario Technological Center">
        Polo Tecnológico Rosario (PTR)
       </a>
       – is located in Rosario within
       <a href="/wiki/La_Siberia" title="La Siberia">
        La Siberia
       </a>
       site. The center focus mainly on research and development of the three following areas: biotechnology, software development and telecommunications. It currently employs 3,500 people and it is expected to grow 100% by 2015 to become one of the largest in Latin America.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
        Culture
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Culture">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Rosario has many cultural activities in many artistic disciplines with national and international reach. The city has produced important personalities in the fields of music, painting, philosophy, politics, poetry, literature, medicine, and law. Among the city's important theaters are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/El_C%C3%ADrculo_Theater" title="El Círculo Theater">
        El Círculo
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sala_Lavard%C3%A9n" title="Sala Lavardén">
        Sala Lavardén
       </a>
       , Broadway, Astengo Auditorium, and La Comedia. A cultural complex known as
       <a href="/wiki/Puerto_de_la_M%C3%BAsica" title="Puerto de la Música">
        Puerto de la Música
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       designed by the modernist architect
       <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Niemeyer" title="Oscar Niemeyer">
        Oscar Niemeyer
       </a>
       (of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brasilia" title="Brasilia">
        Brasilia
       </a>
       fame), is to be built along the banks of the Paraná River. If completed it will be one of the largest centers for musical performance in Latin America. In 2012, after years without progress, it was put on indefinite hold due to financial constraints. January 1995 saw the launch of the Rosario District Fishing Championship, held in the Parana River. 3 years later in 1998, a 10-year-old Lionel Messi was crowned Junior Champion.
      </p>
      <p>
       The city has several
       <a href="/wiki/Museum" title="Museum">
        museums
       </a>
       , including:
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_B._Castagnino_Fine_Arts_Museum" title="Juan B. Castagnino Fine Arts Museum">
        Juan B. Castagnino Fine Arts Museum
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Firma_y_Odilo_Est%C3%A9vez_Municipal_Decorative_Art_Museum" title="Firma y Odilo Estévez Municipal Decorative Art Museum">
        Firma y Odilo Estévez Municipal Decorative Art Museum
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Dr._Julio_Marc_Provincial_Historical_Museum" title="Dr. Julio Marc Provincial Historical Museum">
        Dr. Julio Marc Provincial Historical Museum
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Municipal_Museum_of_the_City_(Rosario)" title="Municipal Museum of the City (Rosario)">
        City Museum
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Contemporary_Art_of_Rosario" title="Museum of Contemporary Art of Rosario">
        Museum of Contemporary Art of Rosario
       </a>
       (MACRo). The
       <a href="/wiki/Dr._%C3%81ngel_Gallardo_Provincial_Natural_Sciences_Museum" title="Dr. Ángel Gallardo Provincial Natural Sciences Museum">
        Dr. Ángel Gallardo Provincial Natural Sciences Museum
       </a>
       was rebuilt after a fire in 2003 and re-opened at a new location in 2006. Rosario also has a public astronomy complex, located in
       <a href="/wiki/Parque_Urquiza_(Rosario)" title="Parque Urquiza (Rosario)">
        Urquiza Park
       </a>
       , which consists of an
       <a href="/wiki/Observatory" title="Observatory">
        observatory
       </a>
       (inaugurated in 1970) and a
       <a href="/wiki/Planetarium" title="Planetarium">
        planetarium
       </a>
       (1984).
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Fundaci%C3%B3n_Italia" title="Fundación Italia">
        Fundación Italia
       </a>
       is a cultural institution created in 1985, as a "cultural bond with Italy". It has organized a
       <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Naples" title="Music of Naples">
        Neapolitan
       </a>
       music concert, performances of
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Madame_Butterfly" title="Madame Butterfly">
         Madame Butterfly
        </a>
       </i>
       and numerous talks about the present and future of Argentina. Among the people invited to give these talks were economists
       <a href="/wiki/Domingo_Cavallo" title="Domingo Cavallo">
        Domingo Cavallo
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alfonso_Prat_Gay" title="Alfonso Prat Gay">
        Alfonso Prat Gay
       </a>
       , renowned scholars
       <a href="/wiki/Beatriz_Sarlo" title="Beatriz Sarlo">
        Beatriz Sarlo
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Economist" title="Economist">
        Silvia Bleichmar
       </a>
       , journalists
       <a href="/wiki/Alejandro_Rozitchner" title="Alejandro Rozitchner">
        Alejandro Rozitchner
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Journalist" title="Journalist">
        Jorge Asís
       </a>
       , filmmaker
       <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Solanas" title="Fernando Solanas">
        Fernando Solanas
       </a>
       and former presidents of Chile (
       <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Lagos" title="Ricardo Lagos">
        Ricardo Lagos
       </a>
       ), Argentina (
       <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Duhalde" title="Eduardo Duhalde">
        Eduardo Duhalde
       </a>
       ), and Uruguay (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luis_Alberto_Lacalle_Herrera" title="Luis Alberto Lacalle Herrera">
        Luis Alberto Lacalle Herrera
       </a>
       ).
      </p>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Racecourse">
        Racecourse
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Racecourse">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The Independence Hippodrome opened on December 8 of 1901, when the first ride meeting was held. The Hippodrome was located in the heart of the Parque de la Independencia and occupied a prominent place in the city's social scene. In 1919, construction began of the Popular Opinion. La Tribuna rises Partners in 1928. Moreover, it had begun the construction of a new box office. In 1941, the Tribune Paddock (formerly Partners Tribune) was demolished. The final podium of professional construidaes, begun in 1972. Independence Hippodrome was the initiator in Argentina night time racing, with lighting facilities for this purpose.
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Tracks
       </dt>
      </dl>
      <p>
       The racecourse features three tracks that are used for entertainment, vacation and skills. The Main Track has 1,794 metres (5,886 ft) of sand. This track is open on Monday, Wednesday and Friday for tests, with Sunday competitions.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Assistant Track 1 has 1,650 m (5,413 ft) with sand, used on Tuesdays, Thursdays, Saturdays and Sundays inclusive for the tournaments and some special courses such as race trot.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Assistant Track 2 has 1,450 m (4,757 ft) of land used to jog and tame.
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Tribunes
       </dt>
      </dl>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Ex-Tribune Partners: with a privileged view of the oval track and focused, this building covers 1,300 m
        <sup>
         2
        </sup>
        (13,990 sq ft) and three levels, the second is a restaurant seating 150 people.
       </li>
       <li>
        Professional-Tribune, has a covered area of 300 m
        <sup>
         2
        </sup>
        (3,229 sq ft). On the ground floor is the technical area and the Commissariat sector.
       </li>
       <li>
        Paddock-Tribune, has covered area of 900 m
        <sup>
         2
        </sup>
        (9,688 sq ft). It has a gambling parlor and a VIP room with buffet area for the fans. It has the office of the Administration and the boxes for journalists.
       </li>
      </ul>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Landmarks">
        Landmarks
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Landmarks">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="National_Flag_Memorial">
        National Flag Memorial
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: National Flag Memorial">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/National_Flag_Memorial_(Argentina)" title="National Flag Memorial (Argentina)">
        National Flag Memorial (Argentina)
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Monumento_Nacional_a_la_Bandera_01.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="2000" height="300" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Monumento_Nacional_a_la_Bandera_01.jpg/200px-Monumento_Nacional_a_la_Bandera_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Monumento_Nacional_a_la_Bandera_01.jpg/300px-Monumento_Nacional_a_la_Bandera_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Monumento_Nacional_a_la_Bandera_01.jpg/400px-Monumento_Nacional_a_la_Bandera_01.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Monumento_Nacional_a_la_Bandera_01.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Argentine Flag Memorial
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Monumento_Bandera_Rosario_Argentina.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Monumento_Bandera_Rosario_Argentina.jpg/200px-Monumento_Bandera_Rosario_Argentina.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Monumento_Bandera_Rosario_Argentina.jpg/300px-Monumento_Bandera_Rosario_Argentina.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Monumento_Bandera_Rosario_Argentina.jpg/400px-Monumento_Bandera_Rosario_Argentina.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Monumento_Bandera_Rosario_Argentina.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Propylaeum (column gallery) of the National Argentine Flag Memorial
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Monumento_a_la_Bandera,_Rosario,_Santa_Fe_(Argentina).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Monumento_a_la_Bandera%2C_Rosario%2C_Santa_Fe_%28Argentina%29.jpg/200px-Monumento_a_la_Bandera%2C_Rosario%2C_Santa_Fe_%28Argentina%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Monumento_a_la_Bandera%2C_Rosario%2C_Santa_Fe_%28Argentina%29.jpg/300px-Monumento_a_la_Bandera%2C_Rosario%2C_Santa_Fe_%28Argentina%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Monumento_a_la_Bandera%2C_Rosario%2C_Santa_Fe_%28Argentina%29.jpg/400px-Monumento_a_la_Bandera%2C_Rosario%2C_Santa_Fe_%28Argentina%29.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Monumento_a_la_Bandera,_Rosario,_Santa_Fe_(Argentina).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Flag Memorial at night
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The National Flag Memorial in Rosario is a monumental complex built near the banks of the Paraná River. It was commissioned in 1944 and inaugurated on June 20, 1957 – the anniversary of the death of
       <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Belgrano" title="Manuel Belgrano">
        Manuel Belgrano
       </a>
       , creator of the Argentine flag, who raised it for the first time on an island in the river on February 27, 1812.
      </p>
      <p>
       The complex has a total area of about 10,000 m
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (107,600 sq ft) and was constructed using stone primarily sourced in the Andes. The structure was designed by the architects
       <a href="/wiki/%C3%81ngel_Guido" title="Ángel Guido">
        Ángel Guido
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Alejandro_Bustillo" title="Alejandro Bustillo">
        Alejandro Bustillo
       </a>
       , and the monument was adorned with works by sculptors
       <a href="/wiki/Lola_Mora" title="Lola Mora">
        Lola Mora
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Barnes" title="Eduardo Barnes">
        Eduardo Barnes
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Bigatti" title="Alfredo Bigatti">
        Alfredo Bigatti
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Fioravanti" title="José Fioravanti">
        José Fioravanti
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Memorial (Monumento) has three parts: the Tower (Torre) or mast, 70 metres (230 ft) high, which commemorates the Revolution of May 1810 and houses Manuel Belgrano's crypt in its base; the Civic Courtyard (Patio Cívico), which symbolizes the effort of the organization of the state (the Courtyard is used for massive open-air shows), and the Triumphal Propylaeum (Propileo Triunfal), representing the nation as organized after the 1853 Constitution. Under the Propylaeum there is the Honor Room for the Flags of America (where the flags of all American nations are displayed).
      </p>
      <p>
       The complex faces Belgrano Avenue, and is delimited by Córdoba and Santa Fe Streets, the latter of which slopes down towards the river at this point. The Propylaeum can be accessed from the pedestrian passage called Pasaje Juramento ("Oath Passage"), which starts at Buenos Aires St. between the municipal building (Palacio de los Leones) and the Cathedral, in front of Plaza 25 de Mayo (May 25 Square). The passage is flanked by statues by famous sculptor Lola Mora.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Memorial and the National Flag Park located in front of it are the seat of the main celebrations of Flag Day on June 20. The 50th anniversary of the inauguration of the complex, in 2007, was marked by a special celebration and by the unveiling of a new lighting system.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7-MSjuN-ilU" rel="nofollow">
        El Puerto de la Música
       </a>
       will be a theater with a total capacity of 30,000 people located by the Paraná River.
      </p>
      <p>
       Architect
       <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Niemeyer" title="Oscar Niemeyer">
        Oscar Niemeyer
       </a>
       came up with the concept by expanding the show from inside the theater to a much larger outside audience. The concrete curvilinear shape building with an area of 215,278 sq ft (20,000.0 m
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       ) is the first design of Oscar Niemeyer in Argentina.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The project will be a distinctive part of Rosario's skyline. Construction will begin at the end of 2010 and is expected to be completed by 2014.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Planetarium">
        Planetarium
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Planetarium">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Located in Urquiza Park, Rosario's Astronomic municipal Complex is one of the principal astronomic centers of the region.
      </p>
      <p>
       The planetarium has a core team, together with its secondary elements, providing an artificial image of the sky, through projections made on a fixed hemispherical dome that functions as a display.
      </p>
      <p>
       The assembly is installed in the Room "Oscar Claudio Caprile", located in the heart of the magnificent building that is shaped like a comet.
      </p>
      <p>
       For its technical characteristics in terms of size, quality of sound and image, and interior comfort, this room is considered among the best in the world.
      </p>
      <p>
       The building in the shape of comet forms a part of the complex that includes the "Prof. Victor Capolongo" observatory and the experimental science museum.
      </p>
      <h5>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="The_observatory">
        The observatory
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: The observatory">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h5>
      <p>
       Municipal Astronomical Observatory "Prof. Victor Capolongo" was inaugurated on June 18, 1970 and named its first director.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Observatory facilitates outreach, teaching and research in the field of astronomy and related sciences and informs the public of phenomena that occur in the sky, such as eclipses, planetary configurations, passages of comets, etc.
      </p>
      <p>
       To that end, the Observatory has installed two telescopes. One refractor Coudé has a 150 mm (5.9 in) aperture and 2,250 mm (88.6 in) focal distance provided with Lyot's monochromatic filter for solar observation. Another reflector type Cassegrain has 300 mm (11.8 in) aperture, constructed by the Carl Zeiss company.
      </p>
      <p>
       There are realized observations and astronomic photography of all the celestial visible objects in Rosario's sky, according to time of year and especially the Sun, the Moon and the planets Jupiter, Saturn, Mars and Venus.
      </p>
      <h5>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Experimental_Science_Museum">
        Experimental Science Museum
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Experimental Science Museum">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h5>
      <p>
       This museum was inaugurated on September 24, 1987. It is the first in Argentina and differs from traditional museums, in that it has equipment and instruments to demonstrate the laws of nature, which can be used by the general public in an interactive way.
      </p>
      <p>
       Thus, visitors of all ages can use telescopes and microscopes, or experiment with lasers, sound mixers, radios of various types, computers, solar cells, etc.
      </p>
      <p>
       To complement this, exhibit panels have photographs and explanatory texts of science and technology: mathematics and computer science, engineering, physics, astronomy, astronautics, geology, chemistry and biology. In addition, an important area is intended for periodic samples, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Space_Age" title="Space Age">
        Space Age
       </a>
       , energy: renewable and rational use, from sand to glass, among others. The museum staff is supported by contributions from the Ministry of Science and Technology Office, the Municipality of Rosario and the contributions made by institutions and individuals.
      </p>
      <p>
       The museum audiovisual projections are made in the Video Sector Science, which has an area called "CIENCIANIÑO" (ChildScience) for children 4 to 10. The museum works in the evening similar to the Planetarium. Educational institutions at all levels are treated in shift assignments.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Statue_of_Che_Guevara">
        Statue of Che Guevara
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Statue of Che Guevara">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The 4 metre-tall bronze statue of
       <a href="/wiki/Che_Guevara" title="Che Guevara">
        Che Guevara
       </a>
       was unveiled on 14 June 2008
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smh_22-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-smh-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       to commemorate his 80th birthday. It is made from 75,000 bronze keys donated by Argentines nationwide
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smh_22-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-smh-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and weighs 2.7 tons. The statue was made by artist Andres Zerneri and is the first such monument to Guevara in his native Argentina.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">

       </span>

         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Argentina" title="Demographics of Argentina">
        Demographics of Argentina
       </a>
      </div>
