      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Districts_of_Rosario_(noted)_(en).svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="990" data-file-width="765" height="233" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Districts_of_Rosario_%28noted%29_%28en%29.svg/180px-Districts_of_Rosario_%28noted%29_%28en%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Districts_of_Rosario_%28noted%29_%28en%29.svg/270px-Districts_of_Rosario_%28noted%29_%28en%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Districts_of_Rosario_%28noted%29_%28en%29.svg/360px-Districts_of_Rosario_%28noted%29_%28en%29.svg.png 2x" width="180"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Districts_of_Rosario_(noted)_(en).svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Diagram of the Municipal Districts of Rosario,
         <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Rosario" title="Districts of Rosario">
          Centre District
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Rosario" title="Districts of Rosario">
          North District
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Rosario" title="Districts of Rosario">
          Northwest District
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Rosario" title="Districts of Rosario">
          West District
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Rosario" title="Districts of Rosario">
          Southwest District
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Rosario" title="Districts of Rosario">
          South District
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Rosario is located in the
       <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Argentina" title="Provinces of Argentina">
        Province
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe_Province" title="Santa Fe Province">
        Santa Fe
       </a>
       , Argentina. This metropolis has a population of about 1.2 million (1,159,004 est.), thus being Argentina's third most populated urban settlement, after
       <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Argentina" title="Córdoba, Argentina">
        Córdoba
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-INDEC_24-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-INDEC-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Greater Rosario comprises Rosario itself (population about 910,000) and a large area around it, spreading in all directions except eastward (because of the Paraná River). Directly to the south it includes the city of
       <a href="/wiki/Villa_Gobernador_G%C3%A1lvez" title="Villa Gobernador Gálvez">
        Villa Gobernador Gálvez
       </a>
       , with a population of about 75,000, at about 10 km (6.2 mi) from Rosario city centre.
      </p>
      <p>
       To the west and south-west there are several smaller towns and cities (
       <a href="/wiki/Funes,_Santa_Fe" title="Funes, Santa Fe">
        Funes
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Rold%C3%A1n,_Santa_Fe" title="Roldán, Santa Fe">
        Roldán
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A9rez,_Santa_Fe" title="Pérez, Santa Fe">
        Pérez
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Soldini,_Santa_Fe" title="Soldini, Santa Fe">
        Soldini
       </a>
       ); Roldán is 23 km (14 mi) from the Rosario city centre. These settlements were incorporated into the metropolis due to their vicinity to major roads leading into Rosario, and many people living there habitually
       <a href="/wiki/Commuting" title="Commuting">
        commute
       </a>
       to Rosario.
      </p>
      <p>
       The farthest end is to the north, following the coast of the river; from Rosario one finds, in succession and usually merging into each other, the towns of
       <a href="/wiki/Granadero_Baigorria" title="Granadero Baigorria">
        Granadero Baigorria
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Capit%C3%A1n_Berm%C3%BAdez" title="Capitán Bermúdez">
        Capitán Bermúdez
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fray_Luis_Beltr%C3%A1n" title="Fray Luis Beltrán">
        Fray Luis Beltrán
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/San_Lorenzo,_Santa_Fe" title="San Lorenzo, Santa Fe">
        San Lorenzo
       </a>
       (already in a different
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Argentina" title="Departments of Argentina">
         departamento
        </a>
       </i>
       , with a population of over 40,000), and
       <a href="/wiki/Puerto_General_San_Mart%C3%ADn" title="Puerto General San Martín">
        Puerto General San Martín
       </a>
       , the last being at a distance of 35 km (22 mi) from Rosario.
      </p>
      <p>
       The north of the Greater Rosario is one end of an area traditionally called
       <i>
        Cordón Industrial
       </i>
       ("Industrial Corridor"), since it was traditionally a heavily industrialized productive region. The prelude to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Argentine_economic_crisis_(1999%E2%80%932002)" title="Argentine economic crisis (1999–2002)">
        economic crisis
       </a>
       in the 1990s largely dismantled the industrial infrastructure and damaged agricultural exports. These sectors were largely revitalized by
       <a href="/wiki/2006_in_Argentina" title="2006 in Argentina">
        2006
       </a>
       as the national economy continued to recover; but high levels of poverty and unemployment persist in the city's western neighborhoods (official surveys indicated that in 2011, 6.5% of the metro area population was under the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Poverty_line" title="Poverty line">
        poverty line
       </a>
       ; and that in 2012, 8.3% of the labor force was unemployed).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eph_5-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-eph-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1876 the total population was 203,509. It doubled in 1908, and yet again in less than two decades; by 1926 Rosario had 407,000 inhabitants, 47% of them foreign, many brought from Europe in the wake of World War I. Most of them were Italian, and among them, a majority from the north-western region of
       <a href="/wiki/Liguria" title="Liguria">
        Liguria
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       As of the 2010 Census, there are 1,193,605 people residing in the city and
       <a href="/wiki/Greater_Rosario" title="Greater Rosario">
        31 surrounding districts
       </a>
       , making Greater Rosario the third-largest metro area in Argentina even as its population growth has leveled off.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2010c_4-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-2010c-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The population density in Rosario proper was 6,680 inhabitants per square kilometer (17,300 per mi
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       ); but, only about 2,400 per km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (6,100 per mi
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       ) in the suburbs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-censo_26-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-censo-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The 2010 Census showed a relatively aged population, as well: with 21% under the age of fifteen and 17% over sixty, the people have an age structure similar to those in many North American cities. They are, likewise, more elderly on average than Argentines as a whole (of whom 25% were under 15 and 14%, over 60).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2010c_4-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2010c-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The ethnic make-up of Rosario changed in the late 19th century, when significant numbers of European immigrants arrived in the city. Prior to this, Rosario's population had been almost completely European-descent in ethnic origin. As
       <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">
        Buenos Aires
       </a>
       was the first landfall in Argentina for many migrant ships coming from Europe in the 1850s and 1890s, Rosario started to experience a diverse influx of people.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The main contributors were
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">
        Italy
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
        France
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">
        Croatia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">
        Poland
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">
        Russia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">
        Romania
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">
        Ukraine
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">
        Balkans
       </a>
       (especially
       <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">
        Greece
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">
        Serbia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">
        Montenegro
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">
        Switzerland
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">
        Germany
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
        United Kingdom
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">
        Ireland
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">
        Scandinavia
       </a>
       (especially
       <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">
        Sweden
       </a>
       ). By the 1910s, 43 percent of the city population was non-native Argentine after immigration rates peaked.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Most immigrants, regardless of origin, settled in the city or around
       <a href="/wiki/Greater_Rosario" title="Greater Rosario">
        Greater Rosario
       </a>
       . However, in the first stages of immigration, some formed colonies (especially
       <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_colonies_in_Argentina" title="Agricultural colonies in Argentina">
        agricultural colonies
       </a>
       ) in different parts of the city, often encouraged by the Argentine government and/or sponsored by private individuals and organizations.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">
        Christianity
       </a>
       is the dominant faith with
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" title="Roman Catholicism">
        Roman Catholicism
       </a>
       as the most practiced, followed by
       <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">
        Protestantism
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">
        Judaism
       </a>
       is the second-most professed religion in the city as Rosario has one of the largest
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Argentina" title="History of the Jews in Argentina">
        Jewish communities in Argentina
       </a>
       . There is also a local
       <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">
        Islamic
       </a>
       society.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Districts">
        Districts
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Districts">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Rosario is divided into six districts, most named by location although the eastmost is called Centre District as it includes the oldest part of the city historicaliy called
       <i>
        Centro
       </i>
       (City Centre). The data given below are from the 2001
       <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">
        census
       </a>
       <small>
        [
        <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Statistics_and_Census_of_Argentina" title="National Institute of Statistics and Census of Argentina">
         INDEC
        </a>
        ]
       </small>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Villa_Hortensia_1.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="2304" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Villa_Hortensia_1.jpg/200px-Villa_Hortensia_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Villa_Hortensia_1.jpg/300px-Villa_Hortensia_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Villa_Hortensia_1.jpg/400px-Villa_Hortensia_1.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Villa_Hortensia_1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Villa_Hortensia_(Rosario)" title="Villa Hortensia (Rosario)">
          Villa Hortensia
         </a>
         , the seat of the North District.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Estaci%C3%B3n_Rosario_Central_1.jpg">

         </div>
         Seat of the Center District, at the former Rosario Central railway station.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>

      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_structure">
        Urban structure
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Urban structure">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Banco_Municipal_de_Rosario_-_1.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2210" data-file-width="1575" height="281" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Banco_Municipal_de_Rosario_-_1.jpg/200px-Banco_Municipal_de_Rosario_-_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Banco_Municipal_de_Rosario_-_1.jpg/300px-Banco_Municipal_de_Rosario_-_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Banco_Municipal_de_Rosario_-_1.jpg/400px-Banco_Municipal_de_Rosario_-_1.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Banco_Municipal_de_Rosario_-_1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The central offices of the Municipal Bank of Rosario
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Centre_District">
        Centre District
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Centre District">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       At Rosario city centre,
       <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba_Street_(Rosario)" title="Córdoba Street (Rosario)">
        Córdoba Street
       </a>
       is the main avenue, it begins at the Flag Memorial Park, climbs towards the district area, and becomes a pedestrian walk for seven blocks, between Plaza 25 de Mayo and Plaza Pringles. Along Córdoba Ave to the west
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Paseo_del_Siglo" title="Paseo del Siglo">
         Paseo del Siglo
        </a>
       </i>
       ("Walk of the Century") was settled, with former houses of wealthy families, finally there is also the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Plaza_San_Mart%C3%ADn_(Rosario)" title="Plaza San Martín (Rosario)">
         San Martín Square
        </a>
       </i>
       , and elsewhere,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Plaza_Montenegro_(Rosario)" title="Plaza Montenegro (Rosario)">
         Plaza Montenegro
        </a>
       </i>
       (on
       <i>
        Peatonal San Martín
       </i>
       , the pedestrian-only four blocks of
       <a href="/wiki/San_Mart%C3%ADn_Street_(Rosario)" title="San Martín Street (Rosario)">
        San Martín Street
       </a>
       ) and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Plaza_Sarmiento_(Rosario)" title="Plaza Sarmiento (Rosario)">
         Plaza Sarmiento
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Oro%C3%B1o_Boulevard" title="Oroño Boulevard">
        Oroño Boulevard
       </a>
       (going north–south) and
       <a href="/wiki/Pellegrini_Avenue_(Rosario)" title="Pellegrini Avenue (Rosario)">
        Pellegrini Avenue
       </a>
       (east–west) mark the boundaries of the town center together with the river. At their confluence starts the
       <a href="/wiki/Parque_de_la_Independencia" title="Parque de la Independencia">
        Parque de la Independencia
       </a>
       , that houses the
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_B._Castagnino_Fine_Arts_Museum" title="Juan B. Castagnino Fine Arts Museum">
        Juan B. Castagnino Fine Arts Museum
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Newell%27s_Old_Boys" title="Newell's Old Boys">
        Newell's Old Boys
       </a>
       football club, and the sports clubs
       <i>
        Provincial
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        Gimnasia y Esgrima
       </i>
       , as well as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Horseracing" title="Horseracing">
        horse racetrack
       </a>
       and the former
       <i>
        Sociedad Rural
       </i>
       (Rural Society).
      </p>
      <p>
       Towards the south, beyond Pellegrini Avenue, there are two more boulevards, 27 de Febrero and Seguí, and avenues Uriburu, Arijón and Battle y Ordóñez. To the west, after Oroño, there are the avenues Ovidio Lagos and Francia, Avellaneda Boulevard and Provincias Unidas Avenue. The main
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Barrio" title="Barrio">
         barrios
        </a>
       </i>
       in the south are
       <a href="/wiki/Barrio" title="Barrio">
        La Tablada
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Barrio" title="Barrio">
        Parque Casado
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Barrio" title="Barrio">
        Las Heras
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Barrio" title="Barrio">
        Las Delicias
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Barrio" title="Barrio">
        Las Flores
       </a>
       . The city ends in the
       <a href="/wiki/Saladillo_Stream" title="Saladillo Stream">
        Saladillo Stream
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Among the districts in the west are
       <a href="/wiki/Barrio_Echesortu" title="Barrio Echesortu">
        Echesortu
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barrio_Belgrano_(Rosario)" title="Barrio Belgrano (Rosario)">
        Belgrano
       </a>
       , Triángulo, Moderno, Godoy and
       <a href="/wiki/Barrio_Fisherton" title="Barrio Fisherton">
        Fisherton
       </a>
       . To the north-east there lie
       <a href="/wiki/Barrio_Pichincha" title="Barrio Pichincha">
        Pichincha
       </a>
       , Ludueña,
       <a href="/wiki/Barrio_Lisandro_de_la_Torre" title="Barrio Lisandro de la Torre">
        Lisandro de la Torre
       </a>
       (home of Rosario Central's stadium) and Empalme Graneros.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rosario_Dolfines_Guaran%C3%AD_Nocturna.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4272" data-file-width="2848" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Rosario_Dolfines_Guaran%C3%AD_Nocturna.jpg/220px-Rosario_Dolfines_Guaran%C3%AD_Nocturna.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Rosario_Dolfines_Guaran%C3%AD_Nocturna.jpg/330px-Rosario_Dolfines_Guaran%C3%AD_Nocturna.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Rosario_Dolfines_Guaran%C3%AD_Nocturna.jpg/440px-Rosario_Dolfines_Guaran%C3%AD_Nocturna.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rosario_Dolfines_Guaran%C3%AD_Nocturna.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Night view of the luxury
         <a href="/wiki/Dolfines_Guaran%C3%AD" title="Dolfines Guaraní">
          Dolfines Guaraní
         </a>
         Towers
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Next to the stadium there is the
       <a href="/wiki/Parque_Alem" title="Parque Alem">
        Parque Alem
       </a>
       , and nearby the Sorrento thermal
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Power_plant" title="Power plant">
        power plant
       </a>
       . To the north lie the districts of
       <a href="/wiki/Barrio_Alberdi" title="Barrio Alberdi">
        Alberdi
       </a>
       , La Florida (with a popular
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beach_resort" title="Beach resort">
        beach resort
       </a>
       of the same name), Parque Field (built under US President John F. Kennedy's Alliance for Progress development plans) and Rucci. The main streets are Alberdi Avenue and its continuation, Rondeau Boulevard (which leads to the
       <a href="/wiki/Rosario-Victoria_Bridge" title="Rosario-Victoria Bridge">
        Rosario-Victoria Bridge
       </a>
       and the city of
       <a href="/wiki/Granadero_Baigorria" title="Granadero Baigorria">
        Granadero Baigorria
       </a>
       ). These are crossed by the avenues Las Tres Vías, Génova, Sorrento and Puccio.
      </p>
      <p>
       An important part of Rosario's urban character is its river bank. The city recovered the river bank of the Paraná not long ago, thanks to a reorganization of terrains formerly owned by the port and the national railroad system. Going from the center immediately north of the port, the river bank is surrounded by a large amount of parks;
       <a href="/wiki/National_Flag_Memorial_(Argentina)" title="National Flag Memorial (Argentina)">
        Argentine flag Memorial
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Parque_de_Espa%C3%B1a" title="Parque de España">
        Parque de España
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Park" title="Park">
        Parque de las Colectividades
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Park" title="Park">
        Parque Sunchales
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Greater_Rosario">
        Greater Rosario
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Greater Rosario">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Through the years, Rosario has spread in all directions. Towards the south, beyond Pellegrini, there are two more boulevards, 27 de Febrero and Seguí, and avenues Uriburu, Arijón and Battle y Ordóñez.To the west, after Oroño, there are the avenues Ovidio Lagos and Francia, Avellaneda Boulevard and Provincias Unidas Avenue. The main neighborhoods in the south are La Tablada, Parque Casado, Las Heras, Las Delicias and Las Flores. The city ends in the
       <a href="/wiki/Saladillo_Stream" title="Saladillo Stream">
        Saladillo Stream
       </a>
       (the natural border with
       <a href="/wiki/Villa_Gobernador_G%C3%A1lvez" title="Villa Gobernador Gálvez">
        Villa Gobernador Gálvez
       </a>
       ). This is just south of the great barrio Grandoli.
      </p>
      <p>
       Among the neighborhoods in the west are
       <a href="/wiki/Barrio_Echesortu" title="Barrio Echesortu">
        Echesortu
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barrio_Belgrano_(Rosario)" title="Barrio Belgrano (Rosario)">
        Belgrano
       </a>
       , Triángulo, Moderno, Godoy and
       <a href="/wiki/Barrio_Fisherton" title="Barrio Fisherton">
        Fisherton
       </a>
       (near the west end of the city, formerly home of hierarchical personnel of English railroad companies established in Rosario). To the north-east there lie the neighborhoods of
       <a href="/wiki/Barrio_Pichincha" title="Barrio Pichincha">
        Pichincha
       </a>
       (a
       <a href="/wiki/Red-light_district" title="Red-light district">
        red-light district
       </a>
       in the early 20th century, now home to an open-air antiquities fair:
       <i>
        Mercado de antigüedades "Feria Retro La Huella"
       </i>
       ), Ludueña,
       <a href="/wiki/Barrio_Lisandro_de_la_Torre" title="Barrio Lisandro de la Torre">
        Lisandro de la Torre
       </a>
       (home of the
       <a href="/wiki/Rosario_Central" title="Rosario Central">
        Rosario Central
       </a>
       football club) and Empalme Graneros; these last three are in the influence area of the
       <a href="/wiki/Ludue%C3%B1a_Stream" title="Ludueña Stream">
        Ludueña Stream
       </a>
       , now contained by underground piping, but until the 1980s a source of floods.
      </p>
      <p>
       Next to the Rosario Central stadium there is a large park,
       <a href="/wiki/Parque_Alem" title="Parque Alem">
        Parque Alem
       </a>
       , and not far from it there stands the Sorrento thermoelectric
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Power_plant" title="Power plant">
        power plant
       </a>
       . North of the Lisandro de la Torre neighborhood there are
       <a href="/wiki/Barrio_Alberdi" title="Barrio Alberdi">
        Alberdi
       </a>
       (formerly an independent town), La Florida (with a popular
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beach_resort" title="Beach resort">
        beach resort
       </a>
       of the same name) and Rucci.
      </p>
      <p>
       The main streets in the north are Alberdi Avenue and its continuation, Rondeau Boulevard (which leads to the north exit of the city, the access to the Rosario-Victoria Bridge and the town of
       <a href="/wiki/Granadero_Baigorria" title="Granadero Baigorria">
        Granadero Baigorria
       </a>
       ). These major arteries are crossed by several avenues: Las Tres Vías, Génova, Sorrento and Puccio.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">
        Transportation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Transportation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Rosario's strategic location is destined to become a significant transportation hub and as the bi-oceanic corridor that links the State of Rio Grande do Sul (Brazil) on the Atlantic Ocean to
       <a href="/wiki/Valpara%C3%ADso" title="Valparaíso">
        Valparaíso
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">
        Chile
       </a>
       ), on the Pacific, an important component in global distribution and the core center of a key corridor in the
       <a href="/wiki/Mercosur" title="Mercosur">
        Mercosur
       </a>
       , the Common Market for the South.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transport">
        Public transport
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Public transport">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Terminal_Mariano_Moreno_(Rosario)_(2).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="986" data-file-width="740" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Terminal_Mariano_Moreno_%28Rosario%29_%282%29.jpg/150px-Terminal_Mariano_Moreno_%28Rosario%29_%282%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Terminal_Mariano_Moreno_%28Rosario%29_%282%29.jpg/225px-Terminal_Mariano_Moreno_%28Rosario%29_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Terminal_Mariano_Moreno_%28Rosario%29_%282%29.jpg/300px-Terminal_Mariano_Moreno_%28Rosario%29_%282%29.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Terminal_Mariano_Moreno_(Rosario)_(2).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Front entrance and clock tower of the Mariano Moreno Bus Terminal in Rosario.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Troleb%C3%BAs_L%C3%ADnea_K_Rosario.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1930" data-file-width="3158" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Troleb%C3%BAs_L%C3%ADnea_K_Rosario.jpg/220px-Troleb%C3%BAs_L%C3%ADnea_K_Rosario.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Troleb%C3%BAs_L%C3%ADnea_K_Rosario.jpg/330px-Troleb%C3%BAs_L%C3%ADnea_K_Rosario.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Troleb%C3%BAs_L%C3%ADnea_K_Rosario.jpg/440px-Troleb%C3%BAs_L%C3%ADnea_K_Rosario.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Troleb%C3%BAs_L%C3%ADnea_K_Rosario.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_Rosario" title="Trolleybuses in Rosario">
          Trolleybus
         </a>
         in the city centre
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:San_Mart%C3%ADn_y_Santa_Fe.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="921" data-file-width="800" height="253" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/San_Mart%C3%ADn_y_Santa_Fe.jpg/220px-San_Mart%C3%ADn_y_Santa_Fe.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/San_Mart%C3%ADn_y_Santa_Fe.jpg/330px-San_Mart%C3%ADn_y_Santa_Fe.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/San_Mart%C3%ADn_y_Santa_Fe.jpg/440px-San_Mart%C3%ADn_y_Santa_Fe.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:San_Mart%C3%ADn_y_Santa_Fe.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The city had a tramway network until 1963.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Rosario public transport system includes buses,
       <a href="/wiki/Trolleybus" title="Trolleybus">
        trolleybuses
       </a>
       and taxicabs.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_Rosario" title="Trolleybuses in Rosario">
        Rosario trolleybus system
       </a>
       consists of only one main trunk line. It is presently operated by a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Government-owned_corporation" title="Government-owned corporation">
        government-owned corporation
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/SEMTUR" title="SEMTUR">
        SEMTUR
       </a>
       (Sociedad del Estado Municipal para el Transporte Urbano de Rosario, "Municipal State Society for Rosario Urban Transport"), as are some of Rosario's other urban bus lines.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Plaza_Sarmiento_(Rosario)" title="Plaza Sarmiento (Rosario)">
        Plaza Sarmiento
       </a>
       is the hub of the city bus system, about 40 urban lines in the metropolitan area that provide service every 5 to 10 minutes.
      </p>
      <p>
       Bus fares are pre-paid by means of either a rechargeable plastic card or a disposable paper
       <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_stripe_card" title="Magnetic stripe card">
        card
       </a>
       with a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magnetic_stripe" title="Magnetic stripe">
        magnetic stripe
       </a>
       which can be bought from
       <a href="/wiki/Post_office" title="Post office">
        post offices
       </a>
       , automatic vending machines, and private businesses. For occasional use, a larger fare can be paid using a
       <a href="/wiki/Coin" title="Coin">
        coin
       </a>
       machine in the bus unit. The interurban lines have differential fares and some allow payment in cash only. The municipal administration is phasing out the paper cards, in favor of the plastic ones, during the second half of 2012.
      </p>
      <p>
       The urban bus fleet was partially renewed during the recovery of the national economy, since 2003, and consists of about 730 units. In 2005 the average age of the buses was 5 years and 11 months. Improvements in the economy have led to increased use of public transport, and comparatively less use of bicycles. According to the Rosario Transportation Office, in 2005 there were about 11 million bus journeys per month,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       by 2007, usage has climbed to 420,000 people every day (12.6 million per month).
      </p>
      <p>
       A significant number of buses run on
       <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">
        natural gas
       </a>
       , as it happens also in Argentina as a whole, since the price of this fuel is quite low compared to the alternatives. The idea to transform all buses to this system did not prosper; most buses run on heavily subsidized
       <a href="/wiki/Diesel_fuel" title="Diesel fuel">
        diesel fuel
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2012
       <a href="/wiki/Bus_lane" title="Bus lane">
        bus lanes
       </a>
       were added to several pairs of parallel streets traversing the downtown area.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Bus stops along these are spaced every three blocks instead of the usual two. For the most part they leave room to only one additional, narrow lane on the left for cars and other vehicles. They can be used for taxis carrying passengers as well. They are exclusive for public transport during weekdays and on Saturday morning; stopping or parking on the affected streets is forbidden, as well as right turns. Their implementation attracted opposition from residents and shop owners but was well received by habitual bus users, since they reduce the time needed to get out of the crowded central area by a noticeable amount.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Rosario has a medium-sized
       <a href="/wiki/Taxicab" title="Taxicab">
        taxi
       </a>
       fleet, with units painted black and outlined in yellow. Some belong to radio-taxi companies and can be reserved by telephone; others only in the streets. As the economy of Argentina recovers, the capacity of the taxi fleet has been strained by higher usage. In September 2005, the Deliberative Council approved the compulsory installation of radio-call systems in all taxi units, but this requirement has not been fulfilled.
      </p>
      <p>
       Rosario is also a major hub for long-distance overland transportation from the Mariano Moreno Bus Terminal,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (
       <i>
        Terminal de Omnibus
       </i>
       ), across from the
       <a href="/wiki/Patio_de_la_Madera" title="Patio de la Madera">
        Patio de la Madera
       </a>
       Convention and Exposition Centre complex, about 15 blocks west of
       <a href="/wiki/Plaza_San_Mart%C3%ADn_(Rosario)" title="Plaza San Martín (Rosario)">
        Plaza San Martin
       </a>
       . The transportation facility serves 73 bus companies in short, medium and long-distance travel, carrying 1,100.000 passengers per month to 784 national and international destinations, which comprise most major domestic cities including
       <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Iguaz%C3%BA" title="Puerto Iguazú">
        Puerto Iguazú
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Salta" title="Salta">
        Salta
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Bariloche" title="Bariloche">
        Bariloche
       </a>
       and international destinations such as
       <a href="/wiki/Asunci%C3%B3n" title="Asunción">
        Asunción
       </a>
       , Paraguay,
       <a href="/wiki/Curitiba" title="Curitiba">
        Curitiba
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">
        Rio de Janeiro
       </a>
       , Brazil and
       <a href="/wiki/Montevideo" title="Montevideo">
        Montevideo
       </a>
       , Uruguay, destinations may be long but white-clad chauffeurs handle comfortable
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coach_(vehicle)" title="Coach (vehicle)">
        long-distance coaches
       </a>
       with modern conveniences.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Rosario_Public_Transportation_Statistics">
        Rosario Public Transportation Statistics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Rosario Public Transportation Statistics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The average amount of time people spend commuting with public transit in Rosario, for example to and from work, on a weekday is 50 min. 9% of public transit riders, ride for more than 2 hours every day. The average amount of time people wait at a stop or station for public transit is 14 min, while 19% of riders wait for over 20 minutes on average every day. The average distance people usually ride in a single trip with public transit is 4.3 km, while 4% travel for over 12 km in a single direction.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Railway">
        Railway
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Railway">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Patio_Parada_Rosario_7.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="2304" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Patio_Parada_Rosario_7.jpg/200px-Patio_Parada_Rosario_7.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Patio_Parada_Rosario_7.jpg/300px-Patio_Parada_Rosario_7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Patio_Parada_Rosario_7.jpg/400px-Patio_Parada_Rosario_7.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Patio_Parada_Rosario_7.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Nuevo_Central_Argentino" title="Nuevo Central Argentino">
          Nuevo Central Argentino
         </a>
         (NCA) freight railway yards.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rosariosur_(4).jpg">

        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">

          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Rosario_Sur_Station" title="Rosario Sur Station">
          Rosario Sur Station
         </a>
         , inaugurated in 2015 to run inter-city services on the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_Mitre_Railway" title="General Mitre Railway">
          General Mitre Railway
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Estaci%C3%B3n_Rosario_Norte_4.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="2304" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Estaci%C3%B3n_Rosario_Norte_4.jpg/200px-Estaci%C3%B3n_Rosario_Norte_4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Estaci%C3%B3n_Rosario_Norte_4.jpg/300px-Estaci%C3%B3n_Rosario_Norte_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Estaci%C3%B3n_Rosario_Norte_4.jpg/400px-Estaci%C3%B3n_Rosario_Norte_4.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Estaci%C3%B3n_Rosario_Norte_4.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Rosario Norte.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Distrito_Centro_Rosario_2.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="1728" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Distrito_Centro_Rosario_2.jpg/150px-Distrito_Centro_Rosario_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Distrito_Centro_Rosario_2.jpg/225px-Distrito_Centro_Rosario_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Distrito_Centro_Rosario_2.jpg/300px-Distrito_Centro_Rosario_2.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Distrito_Centro_Rosario_2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Center Municipal District (former Rosario Central station).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Rosario was one of the main cities chosen by the British and French
       <a href="/wiki/Railway_company" title="Railway company">
        railway companies
       </a>
       that built and operated some of the railways in Argentina during the 19th and early 20th centuries, with more than 15 stations operating in the city. When the entire Argentine railway network was
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Railway_Nationalisation_in_Argentina" title="Railway Nationalisation in Argentina">
        nationalised
       </a>
       during the Presidency of
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Per%C3%B3n" title="Juan Perón">
        Juan Perón
       </a>
       , most of the stations (by then under the administration of State-owned company
       <a href="/wiki/Ferrocarriles_Argentinos" title="Ferrocarriles Argentinos">
        Ferrocarriles Argentinos
       </a>
       ) were closed for
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Passenger_train" title="Passenger train">
        passenger
       </a>
       services to reduce costs, leaving only a few active.
      </p>
      <p>
       As of January 2016, only two stations remain active for passenger services in the city. The following chart describes the total of existing railway stations in Rosario:
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable sortable" style="text-align:left">

        </th>

        </th>
       </tr>
