      <p>
       <b>
        Notes:
       </b>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <sup>
         1
        </sup>
        <i>
         Seat of non-profit "Asociación Rosarina Amigos del Riel"
        </i>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        <sup>
         2
        </sup>
        <i>
         Seat of the Center Municipal District.
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        <sup>
         3
        </sup>
        <i>
         Rosario Audiovisual Center and other uses.
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        <sup>
         4
        </sup>
        <i>
         Re-opened in 1950 as a
         <a href="/wiki/Bus_station" title="Bus station">
          bus station
         </a>
         .
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        <sup>
         5
        </sup>
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/National_University_of_Rosario" title="National University of Rosario">
          National University of Rosario
         </a>
         campus.
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        <sup>
         6
        </sup>
        <i>
         Seat of Cultural Center of Fisherton, lent by NCA to the Municipality of Rosario.
        </i>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cultural_37-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-cultural-37">
          [37]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <sup>
         7
        </sup>
        <i>
         Closed for passenger services in 1977, part of the line granted to
         <a href="/wiki/Nuevo_Central_Argentino" title="Nuevo Central Argentino">
          NCA
         </a>
         with no operations on those stations.
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        <sup>
         8
        </sup>
        <i>
         Long distance passenger services Retiro-Tucumán.
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        <sup>
         9
        </sup>
        <i>
         Closed after being burned during a protest movement (mostly known as "
         <a href="/wiki/Rosariazo" title="Rosariazo">
          Rosariazo
         </a>
         ") against the military dictatorial government, in 1969.
        </i>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
         <a href="#cite_note-38">
          [38]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
         <a href="#cite_note-39">
          [39]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       The passenger train system was severely damaged by the
       <a href="/wiki/Railway_privatisation_in_Argentina" title="Railway privatisation in Argentina">
        privatization
       </a>
       of most railway companies in the early 1990s during
       <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Menem" title="Carlos Menem">
        Carlos Menem
       </a>
       's presidency, but is slowly recovering. The lines operated by
       <a href="/wiki/Nuevo_Central_Argentino" title="Nuevo Central Argentino">
        Nuevo Central Argentino
       </a>
       (NCA) handle most of the
       <a href="/wiki/Cargo" title="Cargo">
        cargo
       </a>
       . Additionally, two
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Private_company" title="Private company">
        private
       </a>
       companies provided limited passenger services to several major cities.
       <a href="/wiki/Trenes_de_Buenos_Aires" title="Trenes de Buenos Aires">
        Trenes de Buenos Aires
       </a>
       (TBA) ran weekly trains south to
       <a href="/wiki/Retiro_Mitre_railway_station" title="Retiro Mitre railway station">
        Retiro
       </a>
       in Buenos Aires and north to
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe,_Argentina" title="Santa Fe, Argentina">
        Santa Fe
       </a>
       . The company
       <a href="/wiki/Ferrocentral" title="Ferrocentral">
        Ferrocentral
       </a>
       also operated weekly trains south to Buenos Aires and northwest to
       <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Argentina" title="Córdoba, Argentina">
        Córdoba
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/San_Miguel_de_Tucum%C3%A1n" title="San Miguel de Tucumán">
        Tucumán
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Nowadays, passenger services to Rosario are being operated by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Government_owned_corporation" title="Government owned corporation">
        State-owned company
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Operadora_Ferroviaria_Sociedad_del_Estado" title="Operadora Ferroviaria Sociedad del Estado">
        Trenes Argentinos
       </a>
       , running trains to
       <a href="/wiki/Rosario_Norte_Station" title="Rosario Norte Station">
        Rosario Norte
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and remodelled
       <a href="/wiki/Rosario_Sur_Station" title="Rosario Sur Station">
        Rosario Sur
       </a>
       station.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Rosario_Oeste_railway_station" title="Rosario Oeste railway station">
        Rosario Oeste
       </a>
       concentrated all the passenger services when railways were nationalised, but currently operates for
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freight_train" title="Freight train">
        freight trains
       </a>
       only.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Projects">
        Projects
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Projects">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires-Rosario-C%C3%B3rdoba_high-speed_railway" title="Buenos Aires-Rosario-Córdoba high-speed railway">
        Buenos Aires-Rosario-Córdoba high-speed railway
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       There was a project to build a
       <a href="/wiki/High-speed_rail" title="High-speed rail">
        high-speed train
       </a>
       between
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires-Rosario-C%C3%B3rdoba_high-speed_railway" title="Buenos Aires-Rosario-Córdoba high-speed railway">
        Buenos Aires-Rosario-Córdoba
       </a>
       , scheduled to be started in 2008, with an inauguration in 2012, that would join Rosario and Buenos Aires in 85 minutes, and would reach Córdoba in another 90 minutes at speeds of up to 320 km/h (199 mph).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However it never was constructed and the project was finally suspended after the controversy it generated among the citizens and the media critics because of the high costs it implicated.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Trams">
        Trams
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Trams">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tramway_Rosario_2.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="2304" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Tramway_Rosario_2.jpg/200px-Tramway_Rosario_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Tramway_Rosario_2.jpg/300px-Tramway_Rosario_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Tramway_Rosario_2.jpg/400px-Tramway_Rosario_2.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tramway_Rosario_2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Tram tracks are still visible in parts of the city.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trams_in_Rosario" title="Trams in Rosario">
        Trams in Rosario
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The city once had a large tramway network with 192 km of track in the centre of the city, however this was abandoned in 1963 after fierce competition from bus transport in the city.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The city now has two heritage tramways, one of which uses vintage trams converted to run on rubber tyres, while the other uses the original trams from the city refurbished to run on rails.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       More recently, a metro system was proposed for the city, though this was shelved in favour of a new urban tramway network. The network is currently in the bidding process, with large firms like
       <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">
        Siemens
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Industrial_and_Commercial_Bank_of_China" title="Industrial and Commercial Bank of China">
        Industrial and Commercial Bank of China
       </a>
       bidding for its construction.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is expected to begin at the recently inaugurated
       <a href="/wiki/Rosario_Sur_Station" title="Rosario Sur Station">
        Rosario Sur Station
       </a>
       and run northwards through the city.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Roadways">
        Roadways
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Roadways">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Rosario is linked to the rest of the country by a number of roads: the Aramburu Highway (southeast, to Buenos Aires),
       <a href="/wiki/National_Route_9_(Argentina)" title="National Route 9 (Argentina)">
        National Route 9
       </a>
       (from Buenos Aires to Rosario and then north and west up to Jujuy and Bolivia), the
       <a href="/wiki/Brigadier_Estanislao_L%C3%B3pez_Highway" title="Brigadier Estanislao López Highway">
        Brigadier Estanislao López Highway
       </a>
       (north, to Santa Fe City), National Route 11 (to the north of Santa Fe, Formosa and Paraguay), National Route 33 (to the southwest of Santa Fe and the province of Buenos Aires, and then through
       <a href="/wiki/National_Route_7_(Argentina)" title="National Route 7 (Argentina)">
        National Route 7
       </a>
       to San Luis, Mendoza and Chile), National Route 34 (north to Santiago del Estero, Tucumán and Bolivia), and National Route 174 (east, to Entre Ríos, over the
       <a href="/wiki/Rosario-Victoria_Bridge" title="Rosario-Victoria Bridge">
        Rosario-Victoria Bridge
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       It is surrounded with an extensive system of two belt-highways called
       <a href="/wiki/National_Route_A008_(Argentina)" title="National Route A008 (Argentina)">
        Circunvalación Motorway
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/National_Route_A012_(Argentina)" title="National Route A012 (Argentina)">
        A012
       </a>
       which in turn set the limits of the city. The beltway is 30 km (19 mi) and was built for traffic to avoid the congested city centre, allowing drivers to bypass the city going around it in a much shorter time. In its 30-kilometre (19 mi) length, it intersects with
       <a href="/wiki/National_Route_9_(Argentina)" title="National Route 9 (Argentina)">
        National Route 9
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Highway" title="Highway">
        National Route 3
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Highway" title="Highway">
        National Route 34
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Highway" title="Highway">
        National Route 11
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Highway" title="Highway">
        National Route 174
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Puente_Rosario_victoria_y_Luna.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="4928" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Puente_Rosario_victoria_y_Luna.JPG/250px-Puente_Rosario_victoria_y_Luna.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Puente_Rosario_victoria_y_Luna.JPG/375px-Puente_Rosario_victoria_y_Luna.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Puente_Rosario_victoria_y_Luna.JPG/500px-Puente_Rosario_victoria_y_Luna.JPG 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Puente_Rosario_victoria_y_Luna.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Rosario-Victoria_Bridge" title="Rosario-Victoria Bridge">
          Rosario-Victoria Bridge
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The official numbering system denotes this road as "A008" but this denomination is mostly unknown by the locals as it is still called "
       <i>
        Avenida de Circunvalación 25 de Mayo
       </i>
       " ("
       <i>
        25 of May Beltway Avenue
       </i>
       ") commemorating the
       <a href="/wiki/May_Revolution" title="May Revolution">
        May Revolution
       </a>
       of 1810. Some sections are named after different personalities by local decree. For example:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The section from the east end on 27 Boulevard to the crossing of Ayacucho Street (old exit to the Rosario-Buenos Aires Highway, now access to Provincial Route 21), is called
        <i>
         "National Route A008 Tte. General Juan Carlos Sánchez"
        </i>
        by decree #232 of 14 May 1981.
       </li>
       <li>
        The section between
        <a href="/wiki/Eva_Per%C3%B3n" title="Eva Perón">
         Eva Perón
        </a>
        Street and the exit to
        <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe,_Argentina" title="Santa Fe, Argentina">
         Santa Fe
        </a>
        (the state capital) on the intersection with Rondeau Boulevard is called
        <i>
         "National Route A008 Dr. Constantino Razzetti"
        </i>
        by law #25769 of 1 September 2003.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/National_Route_A012_(Argentina)" title="National Route A012 (Argentina)">
        A012
       </a>
       is the second beltway at the southeast of the city. It has a semi-circular length centered around the city, running as a long-length beltway. From the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Route_9_(Argentina)" title="National Route 9 (Argentina)">
        National Route 9
       </a>
       junction on km marker 278, in the town of Esther, to the junction with
       <a href="/wiki/National_Route_9_(Argentina)" title="National Route 9 (Argentina)">
        National Route 11
       </a>
       on km marker 326 in the city of
       <a href="/wiki/San_Lorenzo,_Santa_Fe" title="San Lorenzo, Santa Fe">
        San Lorenzo
       </a>
       it runs for 67 km (41.6 mi).
      </p>
      <p>
       This road is popularly known as the
       <i>
        Second Rosario Beltway
       </i>
       , as it borders the metropolitan area of greater Rosario. Through National Decree 1595 of 1979
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       this road switched to federal control. Beforehand this road was called Provincial Route 16.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">
        Airports
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Airports">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rosario_International_Airport" title="Rosario International Airport">
        Rosario International Airport
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aeropuerto_Internacional_Rosario.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Aeropuerto_Internacional_Rosario.jpg/250px-Aeropuerto_Internacional_Rosario.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Aeropuerto_Internacional_Rosario.jpg/375px-Aeropuerto_Internacional_Rosario.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Aeropuerto_Internacional_Rosario.jpg/500px-Aeropuerto_Internacional_Rosario.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aeropuerto_Internacional_Rosario.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Rosario_%E2%80%93_Islas_Malvinas_International_Airport" title="Rosario – Islas Malvinas International Airport">
          Rosario International Airport
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Rosario_%E2%80%93_Islas_Malvinas_International_Airport" title="Rosario – Islas Malvinas International Airport">
        Rosario – Islas Malvinas International Airport
       </a>
       is located 13 km (8 mi) west-northwest from the center of Rosario, a city in the
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe_Province" title="Santa Fe Province">
        Santa Fe Province
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">
        Argentina
       </a>
       . The city of Funes lies directly to the west of the airport, and part of the city limit shares a border with the property of the airport grounds. The airport covers an area of 550
       <a href="/wiki/Hectare" title="Hectare">
        hectares
       </a>
       (1359
       <a href="/wiki/Acre" title="Acre">
        acres
       </a>
       ) and is operated by the Province of Santa Fe.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AIP_51-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AIP-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ORSNA_52-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ORSNA-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The airport serves the
       <a href="/wiki/Greater_Rosario" title="Greater Rosario">
        Greater Rosario
       </a>
       area and is the main hub for
       <a href="/wiki/Sol_L%C3%ADneas_A%C3%A9reas" title="Sol Líneas Aéreas">
        Sol Líneas Aéreas
       </a>
       and is also served by
       <a href="/wiki/Aerol%C3%ADneas_Argentinas" title="Aerolíneas Argentinas">
        Aerolíneas Argentinas
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pluna" title="Pluna">
        Pluna
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Gol_Transportes_A%C3%A9reos" title="Gol Transportes Aéreos">
        Gol Transportes Aéreos
       </a>
       . There are domestic flights within Argentina from Rosario to
       <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">
        Buenos Aires
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Argentina" title="Córdoba, Argentina">
        Córdoba
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mar_del_Plata" title="Mar del Plata">
        Mar del Plata
       </a>
       (via Buenos Aires),
       <a href="/wiki/Mendoza,_Argentina" title="Mendoza, Argentina">
        Mendoza
       </a>
       (vía Córdoba),
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe,_Argentina" title="Santa Fe, Argentina">
        Santa Fe
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Villa_Gesell" title="Villa Gesell">
        Villa Gesell
       </a>
       (via Buenos Aires) cities as well as international services to,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Porto_Alegre,_Brazil" title="Porto Alegre, Brazil">
        Porto Alegre, Brazil
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Punta_del_Este,_Uruguay" title="Punta del Este, Uruguay">
        Punta del Este, Uruguay
       </a>
       (direct flight in summer and via Buenos Aires in fall, winter and spring). The airport is at an altitude of 25 metres (82 ft). Its longest
       <a href="/wiki/Runway" title="Runway">
        runway
       </a>
       measures 3,000 metres (9,843 ft).
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Port">
        Port
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Port">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Rosario" title="Port of Rosario">
        Port of Rosario
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Muelles_de_Rosario_(postal).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="567" data-file-width="998" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Muelles_de_Rosario_%28postal%29.jpg/250px-Muelles_de_Rosario_%28postal%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Muelles_de_Rosario_%28postal%29.jpg/375px-Muelles_de_Rosario_%28postal%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Muelles_de_Rosario_%28postal%29.jpg/500px-Muelles_de_Rosario_%28postal%29.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Muelles_de_Rosario_(postal).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Port of Rosario, c.1910
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Rosario" title="Port of Rosario">
        Port of Rosario
       </a>
       , is an inland port and a major goods-shipping centre of Argentina, located in the city of Rosario,
       <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Argentina" title="Provinces of Argentina">
        province
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe_Province" title="Santa Fe Province">
        Santa Fe
       </a>
       , on the left-hand (western) shore of the Paraná River, about 550 km (340 mi) upstream from the Atlantic Ocean.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       At this point of the course of the Paraná River (Kilometer 420, Mile 260), there is the depth transition between overseas and river navigation. The main channel of the river directly in front of the port has an advantageous configuration that allows preservation of a depth of 10 metres (34 ft) with minor periodic
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dredge" title="Dredge">
        dredging
       </a>
       . This allows for downstream navigation of vessels up to
       <a href="/wiki/Panamax" title="Panamax">
        Panamax
       </a>
       standards. The Paraná is about 600 metres (1,970 ft) wide at Kilometer 418. It becomes 2,000 m (1.2 mi) wide downstream.
      </p>
      <p>
       The port is the largest of a series located in the several cities of the
       <a href="/wiki/Greater_Rosario" title="Greater Rosario">
        Greater Rosario
       </a>
       that lie on the Paraná; the last (northernmost) able of overseas traffic being
       <a href="/wiki/Puerto_General_San_Mart%C3%ADn" title="Puerto General San Martín">
        Puerto General San Martín
       </a>
       (23 km (14 mi). It is part of the Bi-Oceanic Corridor, which joins the Atlantic with the Pacific Ocean via Buenos Aires, Rosario,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba_Province_(Argentina)" title="Córdoba Province (Argentina)">
        Córdoba
       </a>
       , the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuyo,_Argentina" title="Cuyo, Argentina">
        Cuyo
       </a>
       region and
       <a href="/wiki/Valpara%C3%ADso" title="Valparaíso">
        Valparaíso
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">
        Chile
       </a>
       ; going north-south it forms the axis of the
       <a href="/wiki/Paraguay_River" title="Paraguay River">
        Paraguay
       </a>
       -Paraná Hydroway. It directly services the area of Santa Fe that produces a large portion of Argentine exports, and indirectly the whole
       <a href="/wiki/Mercosur" title="Mercosur">
        Mercosur
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Trade_bloc" title="Trade bloc">
        trade bloc
       </a>
       . In 2003 the traffic in the port amounted to 2.9 million tonnes (3,200,000 short tons).
      </p>
      <p>
       Cargo from other parts of Argentina is brought into the port by the railway lines of the
       <a href="/wiki/Nuevo_Central_Argentino" title="Nuevo Central Argentino">
        Nuevo Central Argentino
       </a>
       , communicating with
       <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Argentina" title="Córdoba, Argentina">
        Córdoba
       </a>
       (west) and
       <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%A1rate,_Buenos_Aires" title="Zárate, Buenos Aires">
        Zárate, Buenos Aires
       </a>
       (south), as well as the multiple national and provincial roads and highways that converge in Rosario. Communication with the north-eastern part of the country was enhanced by the 2003 opening of the
       <a href="/wiki/Rosario-Victoria_Bridge" title="Rosario-Victoria Bridge">
        Rosario-Victoria Bridge
       </a>
       , that joins the city with the province of
       <a href="/wiki/Entre_R%C3%ADos_Province" title="Entre Ríos Province">
        Entre Ríos
       </a>
       . The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rosario_International_Airport" title="Rosario International Airport">
        Rosario International Airport
       </a>
       (located 15 km (9 mi) west) has also been refurbished to work with cargo traffic.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">
        Education
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Education">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Escuela_Normal_2_Rosario.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="2304" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Escuela_Normal_2_Rosario.jpg/220px-Escuela_Normal_2_Rosario.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Escuela_Normal_2_Rosario.jpg/330px-Escuela_Normal_2_Rosario.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Escuela_Normal_2_Rosario.jpg/440px-Escuela_Normal_2_Rosario.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Escuela_Normal_2_Rosario.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Teachers' School, on Córdoba Avenue.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Facultad_de_Derecho_Rosario_1.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="2304" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Facultad_de_Derecho_Rosario_1.jpg/220px-Facultad_de_Derecho_Rosario_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Facultad_de_Derecho_Rosario_1.jpg/330px-Facultad_de_Derecho_Rosario_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Facultad_de_Derecho_Rosario_1.jpg/440px-Facultad_de_Derecho_Rosario_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Facultad_de_Derecho_Rosario_1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         National University of Rosario Law School
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Rosario is an important educational centre at a national and international level. It is the home of the
       <a href="/wiki/National_University_of_Rosario" title="National University of Rosario">
        National University of Rosario
       </a>
       (UNR) since 1968, which includes the
       <a href="/wiki/Facultad_de_Derecho_(UNR)" title="Facultad de Derecho (UNR)">
        Law Faculty
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Facultad_de_Ciencias_M%C3%A9dicas_(UNR)" title="Facultad de Ciencias Médicas (UNR)">
        Medicine Faculty
       </a>
       , the Humanities Faculty and an advanced study centre called
       <i>
        Ciudad Universitaria de Rosario
       </i>
       (university city of Rosario) that is home to more than 10 colleges, among them the Faculty of Psychology, the Faculty of Political Sciences, and the Faculty of Architecture. It is also home of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rosario_Regional_Faculty" title="Rosario Regional Faculty">
        Rosario Regional Faculty
       </a>
       , a branch of the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Technological_University" title="National Technological University">
        National Technological University
       </a>
       (UTN). All of these national colleges are free.
      </p>
      <p>
       In the city there are approximately 624 establishments destined for elementary levels and secondary education, the Technical Institute, which depends directly on the UNR. With a solid tradition as for university education, it is head of several academic institutions, and is public, and free access.
      </p>
      <p>
       Currently, there are some 80,000 University students at various institutions around the city, representing approximately 8.5% of the whole inhabitants. This rate is one of the highest in Argentina. In Rosario, nearly 15% of the population benefits from higher education degrees, or have undergone at least some University studies sometime.
      </p>
      <p>
       Rosario has private colleges, as the
       <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Catholic_University_of_Argentina" title="Pontifical Catholic University of Argentina">
        Pontifical Catholic University of Argentina
       </a>
       (UCA), the
       <a href="/wiki/Austral_University_(Argentina)" title="Austral University (Argentina)">
        Austral University
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_Latin_American_Educational_Center" title="University of the Latin American Educational Center">
        University of the Latin American Educational Center
       </a>
       (UCEL), the
       <a href="/wiki/Interamerican_Open_University" title="Interamerican Open University">
        Interamerican Open University
       </a>
       (UAI), the Italian University of Rosario (IUNIR), the San Martin University and the University of Concepcion del Uruguay which are private institutions.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Language">
        Language
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Language">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Rosario is the third largest urban center where
       <a href="/wiki/Rioplatense_Spanish" title="Rioplatense Spanish">
        Rioplatense Spanish
       </a>
       is spoken, after Buenos Aires and Montevideo. The local language evidences the typical linguistic features that characterize this
       <a href="/wiki/Dialect" title="Dialect">
        dialect
       </a>
       , notably the
       <a href="/wiki/Voseo" title="Voseo">
        voseo
       </a>
       (use of
       <i>
        vos
       </i>
       instead of
       <i>
        tú
       </i>
       as pronoun for the second person singular) and the
       <i>
        sheismo
       </i>
       (form of
       <a href="/wiki/Ye%C3%ADsmo" title="Yeísmo">
        yeísmo
       </a>
       where
       <i>
        ll-
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        y-
       </i>
       are pronounced as a
       <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_postalveolar_fricative" title="Voiceless postalveolar fricative">
        voiceless
       </a>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ʃ]
       </span>
       ). Although the
       <i>
        español rosarino
       </i>
       does not differ substantially from the other variants of the same dialect, it presents particularities easily noticeable by those who live in the other main populated areas of the region.
      </p>
      <p>
       One of the most notable characteristics of the language of Rosario's area of influence is the process of aspiration and disappearance of the
       <i>
        -s
       </i>
       . When the
       <i>
        -s
       </i>
       is in implosive position, end of syllable or word followed by consonant, its sound becomes a soft and voiceless aspiration [h] (the word
       <i>
        obispo
       </i>
       is pronounced
       <b>
        o̞ˈβihpo̞
       </b>
       ). In the popular and vulgar language, the final
       <i>
        -s
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        -r
       </i>
       , or
       <i>
        -d
       </i>
       are sometimes suppressed, although this phenomenon is commonly associated to sociocultural groups of lower formal education.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Just as in Buenos Aires, the
       <i>
        voseo
       </i>
       is pronominal and verbal. The pronoun
       <i>
        tú
       </i>
       and its associated verbal forms are inexistent (which is not the case of the Montevideo variant) The tendency to add a final
       <i>
        -s
       </i>
       to the verbal forms of the second person plural (
       <i>
        vos fuistes
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        vos vinistes
       </i>
       ), which is rather common in Buenos Aires, is very unusual among Rosario natives. The
       <a href="/wiki/Intonation_(linguistics)" title="Intonation (linguistics)">
        intonation
       </a>
       in Rosario is generally more neutral and monotonous than that of Buenos Aires.
      </p>
      <p>
       Even though the
       <a href="/wiki/Lexicon" title="Lexicon">
        lexicon
       </a>
       of Rosario and Buenos Aires is effectively identical, there are numerous terms and idioms that Rosario shares with the rest of the country (even areas where a different dialect prevails) but not with the capital, as well as other words and expressions that are unique to the
       <i>
        rosarino
       </i>
       speech, both formal and informal.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Rosarigasino" title="Rosarigasino">
         Rosarigasino
        </a>
       </i>
       is a type of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jerigonza" title="Jerigonza">
        Jerigonza
       </a>
       (game of words) that originated in the city and was rather common in the informal speech during the 20th century. Although it has fallen into disuse, it has become a language of
       <a href="/wiki/Cult" title="Cult">
        cult
       </a>
       among certain local groups.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">
        Sports
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Sports">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Messi_Copa_America_2011.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="484" data-file-width="363" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Messi_Copa_America_2011.jpg/170px-Messi_Copa_America_2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Messi_Copa_America_2011.jpg/255px-Messi_Copa_America_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Messi_Copa_America_2011.jpg/340px-Messi_Copa_America_2011.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Messi_Copa_America_2011.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Messi" title="Lionel Messi">
          Lionel Messi
         </a>
         , born in Rosario in 1987.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Rosario is the home of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_(soccer)" title="Football (soccer)">
        football
       </a>
       clubs
       <a href="/wiki/Rosario_Central" title="Rosario Central">
        Rosario Central
       </a>
       (founded 1889) and
       <a href="/wiki/Newell%27s_Old_Boys" title="Newell's Old Boys">
        Newell's Old Boys
       </a>
       (founded 1903). Both play in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primera_Divisi%C3%B3n_Argentina" title="Primera División Argentina">
        Primera División Argentina
       </a>
       . Central has won 4 National championships (in 1971, 1973, 1980 and in 1987), 5 National cups (1913, 1915, two cups in 1916, and in 1920),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and 1 international title: the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conmebol_Cup" title="Conmebol Cup">
        Conmebol Cup
       </a>
       (precursor of the current
       <a href="/wiki/Copa_Sudamericana" title="Copa Sudamericana">
        Copa Sudamericana
       </a>
       )
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in 1995. Newell's has 6 National championships (in 1974, 1988, 1991, 1992, 2004 and in 2013) and 3 National cups (in 1911, 1921 and in 1949). Rosario's other football clubs are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Club_Atl%C3%A9tico_Central_C%C3%B3rdoba" title="Club Atlético Central Córdoba">
        Club Atlético Central Córdoba
       </a>
       , currently playing in
       <a href="/wiki/Primera_C" title="Primera C">
        Primera C
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Club_Atl%C3%A9tico_Tiro_Federal_Argentino" title="Club Atlético Tiro Federal Argentino">
        Club Atlético Tiro Federal Argentino
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Torneo_Argentino_A" title="Torneo Argentino A">
        Torneo Argentino A
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Argentino_de_Rosario" title="Argentino de Rosario">
        Argentino de Rosario
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Primera_D" title="Primera D">
        Primera D
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       It is also the hometown of Argentine internationals
       <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Messi" title="Lionel Messi">
        Lionel Messi
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/%C3%81ngel_Di_Mar%C3%ADa" title="Ángel Di María">
        Ángel Di María
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Maxi_Rodr%C3%ADguez" title="Maxi Rodríguez">
        Maximiliano Rodríguez
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A9sar_Delgado" title="César Delgado">
        César Delgado
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ezequiel_Lavezzi" title="Ezequiel Lavezzi">
        Ezequiel Lavezzi
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mauro_Icardi" title="Mauro Icardi">
        Mauro Icardi
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ezequiel_Garay" title="Ezequiel Garay">
        Ezequiel Garay
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Luciana_Aymar" title="Luciana Aymar">
        Luciana Aymar
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Imhoff" title="Juan Imhoff">
        Juan Imhoff
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nicol%C3%A1s_Vergallo" title="Nicolás Vergallo">
        Nicolás Vergallo
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_Senatore" title="Leonardo Senatore">
        Leonardo Senatore
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The city also received international attention as the host of the
       <a href="/wiki/1982_Southern_Cross_Games" title="1982 Southern Cross Games">
        II South American Games
       </a>
       in 1982, as one of the host cities of the
       <a href="/wiki/1978_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1978 FIFA World Cup">
        1978 FIFA World Cup
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/1982_FIVB_Volleyball_Men%27s_World_Championship" title="1982 FIVB Volleyball Men's World Championship">
        1982 FIVB Volleyball Men's World Championship
       </a>
       , the 1993
       <a href="/wiki/FIVB_Volleyball_Men%27s_U21_World_Championship" title="FIVB Volleyball Men's U21 World Championship">
        FIVB Volleyball Men's U21 World Championship
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/2001_FIFA_World_Youth_Championship" title="2001 FIFA World Youth Championship">
        2001 FIFA World Youth Championship
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1990_Basketball_World_Cup" title="1990 Basketball World Cup">
        1990 Basketball World Cup
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Rosario also bid for the
       <a href="/wiki/2019_Pan_American_Games" title="2019 Pan American Games">
        2019 Pan American Games
       </a>
       but the Argentine Olympic Committee (COA) voted to support
       <a href="/wiki/La_Punta,_San_Luis" title="La Punta, San Luis">
        La Punta
       </a>
       instead.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Rosario is also the second choice site for
       <a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_rugby_union_team" title="Argentina national rugby union team">
        Argentine
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">
        rugby
       </a>
       tests, after
       <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">
        Buenos Aires
       </a>
       . Famous rugby clubs from the city include
       <a href="/wiki/Club_Atl%C3%A9tico_del_Rosario" title="Club Atlético del Rosario">
        Club Atlético del Rosario
       </a>
       – one of the four
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uni%C3%B3n_Argentina_de_Rugby" title="Unión Argentina de Rugby">
        UAR
       </a>
       founding clubs – and also
       <a href="/wiki/Jockey_Club_de_Rosario" title="Jockey Club de Rosario">
        Jockey Club de Rosario
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Duendes_Rugby_Club" title="Duendes Rugby Club">
        Duendes Rugby Club
       </a>
       , both former winners of the
       <a href="/wiki/Nacional_de_Clubes" title="Nacional de Clubes">
        Nacional de Clubes
       </a>
       title. The city hosted the
       <a href="/wiki/2010_IRB_Junior_World_Championship" title="2010 IRB Junior World Championship">
        2010 IRB Junior World Championship
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/2010_Women%27s_Hockey_World_Cup" title="2010 Women's Hockey World Cup">
        2010 Women's Hockey World Cup
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/2004_Women%27s_Hockey_Champions_Trophy" title="2004 Women's Hockey Champions Trophy">
        2004
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/2012_Women%27s_Hockey_Champions_Trophy" title="2012 Women's Hockey Champions Trophy">
        2012
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Hockey_Champions_Trophy" title="Hockey Champions Trophy">
        Champions Trophy
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Women%27s_FIH_Hockey_World_League_Final" title="2014–15 Women's FIH Hockey World League Final">
        2014–15 Women's FIH Hockey World League Final
       </a>
       were played in this city.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2014 the city hosted the
       <a href="/wiki/Inline_speed_skating#World_Championships" title="Inline speed skating">
        Inline speed skating World Championship
       </a>
       at
       <a href="/wiki/Parque_de_la_Independencia" title="Parque de la Independencia">
        Parque de la Independencia
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and in 2015 it hosted the men's, women's and juniors'
       <a href="/wiki/FIRS_Inline_Hockey_World_Championships" title="FIRS Inline Hockey World Championships">
        FIRS Inline Hockey World Championships
       </a>
       at
       <a href="/wiki/Club_Atl%C3%A9tico_Provincial" title="Club Atlético Provincial">
        Club Atlético Provincial's
       </a>
       indoor arena.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Rosario also hosted the
       <a href="/wiki/2017_World_Archery_Youth_Championships" title="2017 World Archery Youth Championships">
        2017 World Archery Youth Championships
       </a>
       , and will host the
       <a href="/wiki/2018_FIBA_Under-17_Basketball_World_Cup" title="2018 FIBA Under-17 Basketball World Cup">
        2018 FIBA Under-17 Basketball World Cup
       </a>
       , and the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=2019_South_American_Beach_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="2019 South American Beach Games (page does not exist)">
        2019 South American Beach Games
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Motorsports">
        Motorsports
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Motorsports">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The city was the starting point for the
       <a href="/wiki/2014_Dakar_Rally" title="2014 Dakar Rally">
        2014 Dakar Rally
       </a>
       , as well as the finishing point in
       <a href="/wiki/2016_Dakar_Rally" title="2016 Dakar Rally">
        2016
       </a>
       . It also hosted the
       <a href="/wiki/2015_World_RX_of_Argentina" title="2015 World RX of Argentina">
        2015 World RX of Argentina
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Events">
        Events
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Events">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:World%27s_longest_flag,_Argentina_-_3.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="2304" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/World%27s_longest_flag%2C_Argentina_-_3.jpg/200px-World%27s_longest_flag%2C_Argentina_-_3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/World%27s_longest_flag%2C_Argentina_-_3.jpg/300px-World%27s_longest_flag%2C_Argentina_-_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/World%27s_longest_flag%2C_Argentina_-_3.jpg/400px-World%27s_longest_flag%2C_Argentina_-_3.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:World%27s_longest_flag,_Argentina_-_3.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Participants carry the national colors on Flag Day (June 20).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Festival_Latinoamericano_de_Video_Rosario" title="Festival Latinoamericano de Video Rosario">
          Festival Latinoamericano de Video Rosario
         </a>
        </i>
        (Rosario Latin American Video Festival). Annual event (September), starting in 1994.
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Encuentro_Internacional_de_Escultura_en_Madera-Piedra-Hierro_de_Rosario" title="Encuentro Internacional de Escultura en Madera-Piedra-Hierro de Rosario">
          Encuentro Internacional de Escultura en Madera-Piedra-Hierro de Rosario
         </a>
        </i>
        (International Meeting of Wood-Stone-Iron Sculpture in Rosario). Annual event (September/October), since 1993.
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Encuentro_y_Fiesta_Nacional_de_Colectividades_(Rosario,_Argentina)" title="Encuentro y Fiesta Nacional de Colectividades (Rosario, Argentina)">
          Encuentro y Fiesta Nacional de Colectividades
         </a>
        </i>
        (Communities Meeting and National Celebration). Annual event, starting in 1985, showcasing music, song, dance, cuisine and customs of foreign communities in Argentina, in the ample room provided by the
        <i>
         Parque Nacional a la Bandera
        </i>
        (National Flag Park). Usually held in November; in 2004 it was postponed to the beginning of December in order to avoid overlap with the
        <a href="/wiki/Third_International_Congress_of_the_Spanish_Language" title="Third International Congress of the Spanish Language">
         Third International Congress of the Spanish Language
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Festival_Internacional_de_Poes%C3%ADa_de_Rosario" title="Festival Internacional de Poesía de Rosario">
          Festival Internacional de Poesía de Rosario
         </a>
        </i>
        (International Poetry Festival). Annual event since 1993 (November).
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         Festival Iberoamericano de Cine de Rosario
        </i>
        (Ibero-American Film Festival). Annual event since 2003 (November).
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Leyendas" title="Leyendas">
          Leyendas
         </a>
        </i>
        ("Legends"). A cartoon, role-playing and science fiction convention. Annually since 1999, usually in autumn (April/May), sometimes in spring (November).
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Geography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Rosario" title="Geography of Rosario">
        Geography of Rosario
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Departamento_Rosario_(Santa_Fe_-_Argentina).png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1747" data-file-width="1033" height="304" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Departamento_Rosario_%28Santa_Fe_-_Argentina%29.png/180px-Departamento_Rosario_%28Santa_Fe_-_Argentina%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Departamento_Rosario_%28Santa_Fe_-_Argentina%29.png/270px-Departamento_Rosario_%28Santa_Fe_-_Argentina%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Departamento_Rosario_%28Santa_Fe_-_Argentina%29.png/360px-Departamento_Rosario_%28Santa_Fe_-_Argentina%29.png 2x" width="180"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Departamento_Rosario_(Santa_Fe_-_Argentina).png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Rosario metropolitan area in the Province of Santa Fe
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The city of Rosario measures 178.69 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (69.0 sq mi), not all of them are fully urbanized. Its extreme points are:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">
         Latitude
        </a>
        :
        <a href="/wiki/Circle_of_latitude" title="Circle of latitude">
         parallels
        </a>
        32°52′18″ and 33°02′22″ South.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Longitude" title="Longitude">
         Longitude
        </a>
        :
        <a href="/wiki/Meridian_(astronomy)" title="Meridian (astronomy)">
         meridians
        </a>
        60°36′44″ and 60°47′46″ West.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       The geographical center is approximately at
       <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion">
        <a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;params=32_57_2_S_60_42_15_W_">
         <span class="geo-default">
          <span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">
           <span class="latitude">
            32°57′2″S
           </span>
           <span class="longitude">
            60°42′15″W
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
         <span class="geo-multi-punct">
          ﻿ / ﻿
         </span>
         <span class="geo-nondefault">
          <span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">
           32.95056°S 60.70417°W
          </span>
          <span style="display:none">
           ﻿ /
           <span class="geo">
            -32.95056; -60.70417
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
        </a>
       </span>
       (
       <i>
        see also
       </i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_cities_by_latitude#30_S" title="List of cities by latitude">
        other cities on the same latitude
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       The city is located on a smoothly undulated plain typical of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pampa" title="Pampa">
        Pampas
       </a>
       , between 22.5 and 24.6 metres
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" title="Above mean sea level">
        above mean sea level
       </a>
       ; the original settlement rests on the
       <a href="/wiki/Ravine" title="Ravine">
        ravine
       </a>
       on the right-hand shore of the Paraná, opposite a group of islands of the
       <a href="/wiki/Paran%C3%A1_Delta" title="Paraná Delta">
        Paraná Delta
       </a>
       which are partly in the jurisdiction of the province of
       <a href="/wiki/Entre_R%C3%ADos_Province" title="Entre Ríos Province">
        Entre Ríos
       </a>
       . The nearest city across the river's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flood_plain" title="Flood plain">
        flood plain
       </a>
       (60 km) is
       <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_Entre_R%C3%ADos" title="Victoria, Entre Ríos">
        Victoria, Entre Ríos
       </a>
       , linked to Rosario by the
       <a href="/wiki/Rosario-Victoria_Bridge" title="Rosario-Victoria Bridge">
        Rosario-Victoria Bridge
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Rosario lies on the
       <a href="/wiki/Ravine" title="Ravine">
        ravine
       </a>
       of the right-hand shore of the Paraná, about 24 metres (79 ft)
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" title="Above mean sea level">
        above mean sea level
       </a>
       , in a place with a natural slope to the low shore. The point of origin of the city is
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Plaza_25_de_Mayo_(Rosario)" title="Plaza 25 de Mayo (Rosario)">
         Plaza 25 de Mayo
        </a>
       </i>
       ("
       <a href="/wiki/May_Revolution" title="May Revolution">
        May 25
       </a>
       Square"), now surrounded by the municipality (
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Palacio_de_los_Leones" title="Palacio de los Leones">
         Palacio de los Leones
        </a>
       </i>
       ), the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basilica_Cathedral_of_Our_Lady_of_the_Rosary" title="Basilica Cathedral of Our Lady of the Rosary">
        Basilica Cathedral of Our Lady of the Rosary
       </a>
       , the Central Post Office, the
       <a href="/wiki/Firma_y_Odilo_Est%C3%A9vez_Municipal_Decorative_Art_Museum" title="Firma y Odilo Estévez Municipal Decorative Art Museum">
        Decorative Art Museum
       </a>
       and a building called
       <i>
        La Bola de Nieve
       </i>
       ("The Snowball"). Between the Cathedral and the municipal building is
       <i>
        Pasaje Juramento
       </i>
       ("Oath Passage"), leading to the Flag Memorial. The streets mostly follow a regular
       <a href="/wiki/Checkerboard" title="Checkerboard">
        checkerboard
       </a>
       pattern.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Climate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Clima_Rosario_(Argentina).PNG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="604" data-file-width="974" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Clima_Rosario_%28Argentina%29.PNG/240px-Clima_Rosario_%28Argentina%29.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Clima_Rosario_%28Argentina%29.PNG/360px-Clima_Rosario_%28Argentina%29.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Clima_Rosario_%28Argentina%29.PNG/480px-Clima_Rosario_%28Argentina%29.PNG 2x" width="240"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Clima_Rosario_(Argentina).PNG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Climate chart
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Rosario area has a
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pampa" title="Pampa">
         Pampean
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">
        humid subtropical climate
       </a>
       (Köppen climate classification: Cfa/Cwa),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Climate-Data.org_68-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Climate-Data.org-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and is well known for its changeable weather conditions. The city has average temperatures of 23.7 °C (74.7 °F) maximum and 11.8 °C (53.2 °F) minimum. The annual rainfall is 1,038 mm (40.9 in).
      </p>
      <p>
       Rosario is usually warmer than other mainland Argentine capital cities in the winter. The lowest average in winter is 4.4 °C (40 °F). This is due in part to the city's flat topography, its situation on the Paraná River bank, and the presence of high density of urbanization. Those conditions have created a microclimate known as
       <a href="/wiki/Urban_heat_island" title="Urban heat island">
        urban heat island
       </a>
       that often means that the city is significantly warmer than its surrounding rural areas.
      </p>
      <p>
       The temperature difference usually is larger at night than during the day and larger in winter than in summer, and is most apparent when winds are weak. However, snowfalls are extremely rare: the most recent occurrence of sleet in the CBD was on 9 July 2007. During the spring, Rosario commonly enjoys extended periods of warm weather and clear skies. On average, Rosario has average day-night temperatures of 23–10 °C (73–50 °F). The city experiences hot and humid summer days, with maximum temperatures above 35 °C (95 °F), when northerly winds blow humid air from Brazil. The record high temperature is 40.5 °C (104.9 °F) on January 9, 2006 while the record low is −7.8 °C (18 °F) (repeated three times: June 13 and 14, 1967, and August 4, 1995).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-meteoclimat_69-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-meteoclimat-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ORA_70-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ORA-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      </table>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Broadcasting_and_communications">
        Broadcasting and communications
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rosario,_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Broadcasting and communications">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Telecom_sede_Rosario.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="2304" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Telecom_sede_Rosario.jpg/200px-Telecom_sede_Rosario.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Telecom_sede_Rosario.jpg/300px-Telecom_sede_Rosario.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Telecom_sede_Rosario.jpg/400px-Telecom_sede_Rosario.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Telecom_sede_Rosario.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Rosario offices of
         <a href="/wiki/Telecom_Argentina" title="Telecom Argentina">
          Telecom Argentina
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Diario_La_Capital_Rosario_1.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="2304" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Diario_La_Capital_Rosario_1.jpg/200px-Diario_La_Capital_Rosario_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Diario_La_Capital_Rosario_1.jpg/300px-Diario_La_Capital_Rosario_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Diario_La_Capital_Rosario_1.jpg/400px-Diario_La_Capital_Rosario_1.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Diario_La_Capital_Rosario_1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Headquarters of
         <a href="/wiki/La_Capital" title="La Capital">
          La Capital
         </a>
         newspaper.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       As for television, Rosario has two private local
       <a href="/wiki/Television_channel" title="Television channel">
        channels
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Channel_3_-_Rosario" title="Channel 3 - Rosario">
        Canal 3
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Channel_5_-_Rosario" title="Channel 5 - Rosario">
        Canal 5
       </a>
       (the latter is part of the national network
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Telef%C3%A9" title="Telefé">
        Telefé
       </a>
       ), and a relay station for the public national station,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canal_7_Argentina" title="Canal 7 Argentina">
        Canal 7 Argentina
       </a>
       . Besides, there are three cable TV networks (the national ones
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grupo_Clar%C3%ADn" title="Grupo Clarín">
        Cablevisión and Multicanal
       </a>
       , and a local network, Cablehogar), which support two local channels, Canal 4 Noticias and Canal 6.
      </p>
      <p>
       There are four
       <a href="/wiki/Amplitude_modulation" title="Amplitude modulation">
        AM
       </a>
       radio stations: three private (licensed by the state) ones,
       <i>
        LT3
       </i>
       <i>
        Radio 2
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        LT2
       </i>
       ), and
       <i>
        LT8
       </i>
       , and one public,
       <i>
        Radio Nacional Rosario
       </i>
       , property of the national state. Among the multitude (above 200) of
       <a href="/wiki/Frequency_modulation" title="Frequency modulation">
        FM
       </a>
       stations some notable ones are
       <i>
        FM Vida
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Estación del Siglo
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        FM Del Rosario
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Cristal FM
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Radio Hollywood
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Fisherton-CNN
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Continental Rosario
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Radio 10 Rosario
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Radiofónica
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Clásica Rosario
       </i>
       , etc.
      </p>
      <p>
       The city has three notable newspapers:
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/La_Capital" title="La Capital">
         La Capital
        </a>
       </i>
       (Argentina's oldest newspaper, founded in 1867, and still published today),
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rosario/12" title="Rosario/12">
         Rosario/12
        </a>
       </i>
       (founded in 1991), and
       <i>
        El Ciudadano &amp; La Región
       </i>
       (founded in 1999).
      </p>
      <p>
       Rosario is located at the center of Argentina's
       <a href="/wiki/Optical_fiber" title="Optical fiber">
        optical fiber
       </a>
       ring. The main data transport companies offer all their services in the city, from public phones to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mobile_telephone" title="Mobile telephone">
        mobile
       </a>
       networks and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broadband_Internet_access" title="Broadband Internet access">
        broadband Internet access
       </a>
       through
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Digital_Subscriber_Line" title="Digital Subscriber Line">
        DSL
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cable_modem" title="Cable modem">
        cable modem
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Wi-Fi" title="Wi-Fi">
        Wi-Fi
       </a>
       , and including public Internet navigation centers (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Internet_cafe" title="Internet cafe">
        cybercafes
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       About 96% of homes have a domestic
       <a href="/wiki/Communications_in_Argentina" title="Communications in Argentina">
        telephone line
       </a>
       , giving a total of 472,170 lines; cell phone usage has also become pervasive, as happened in Argentina as a whole since the beginning of the 21st century, reaching over 86% of the residents (866,000 mobile lines in July 2004). This demand, boosted by low prices and sale promotions, and coupled with restrictions on the installation of antennas and alleged lack of investment by the providers, sometimes degrades the quality of the service. Most notably, the mobile network collapsed almost completely in the celebrations of
       <a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">
        Christmas
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Day" title="New Year's Day">
        New Year's Day
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/D%C3%ADa_del_Amigo" title="Día del Amigo">
        Friend's Day
       </a>
       in 2004 and 2005.
      </p>

      <h3>
       <span id="Twin_towns_.E2.80.93_Sister_cities">

       <span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_–_Sister_cities">

       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

        </span>
